## Memory

- Skipped: `false`

### Prompt

```text
## Guidelines
You need to extract and summarize useful insights in the format of memory items based on comparing the successful and unsuccessful solution attempts below.
The goal of summarized memory items is to be GENERALIZABLE and TRANSFERABLE — each insight must be useful not just for this problem, but for a broad class of similar problems. Write each memory as advice that would help someone who has never seen this specific problem.

## Important notes
- You must first think about why certain attempts succeeded and others failed, then summarize the insights.
- You can extract multiple memory items from the comparison. Each should capture a distinct, independent insight.
- Prioritize GENERAL META-REASONING techniques over object-level hints. Favor principles about representation choice, constraint formalization, invariant selection, validation, decomposition, debugging, or algorithm selection.
- Convert failure observations into POSITIVE reusable guidance. Do not write memories that are just restatements of one wrong step.
- Do NOT mention specific values, answers, variable names, or problem-specific details. Every memory item must stand on its own as a general problem-solving principle or technique that transfers across different problems in the same domain.
- Avoid narrow one-off tricks unless they clearly transfer to a recurring class of problems. Fewer high-quality memories are better than many repetitive ones.
- Emphasize high-level strategies that would still make sense on a different problem in the same domain.

## Examples of good meta-reasoning memories
- Title: Constraint-First Reformulation
  Description: Turn informal requirements into explicit constraints before solving.
  Content: Rewrite vague conditions as equations, inequalities, parity rules, or state constraints. Use those formal constraints to guide the solution and reject invalid branches early.
- Title: Validate Risky Transformations
  Description: Check any step that can introduce invalid candidates against the original problem.
  Content: Squaring, dividing, relaxing constraints, or compressing state can create artifacts that look valid only in the transformed setting. Add a direct verification pass against the original conditions before committing to an answer.
- Title: Model the Smallest Faithful State
  Description: Reduce the problem to the minimal state that still determines future decisions.
  Content: If only parity, remainder class, last element, or turn matters, build the reasoning or DP around that reduced state instead of the full object. This shrinks search and makes transitions easier to verify.

### Problem
We have a grid with H rows and W columns.
Let (i,j) denote the square at the i-th row from the top and j-th column from the left.
Each square in the grid is one of the following: the start square, the goal square, an empty square, a wall square, and a candy square.
(i,j) is represented by a character A_{i,j}, and is the start square if A_{i,j}= S, the goal square if A_{i,j}= G, an empty square if A_{i,j}= ., a wall square if A_{i,j}= #, and a candy square if A_{i,j}= o.
Here, it is guaranteed that there are exactly one start, exactly one goal, and at most 18 candy squares.
Takahashi is now at the start square.
He can repeat moving to a vertically or horizontally adjacent non-wall square.
He wants to reach the goal square in at most T moves.
Determine whether it is possible.
If it is possible, find the maximum number of candy squares he can visit on the way to the goal square, where he must finish.
Each candy square counts only once, even if it is visited multiple times.

Input

The input is given from Standard Input in the following format:
H W T
A_{1,1}A_{1,2}\dots A_{1,W}
\vdots
A_{H,1}A_{H,2}\dots A_{H,W}

Output

If it is impossible to reach the goal square in at most T moves, print -1.
Otherwise, print the maximum number of candy squares that can be visited on the way to the goal square, where Takahashi must finish.

Constraints


- 1\leq H,W \leq 300
- 1 \leq T \leq 2\times 10^6
- H, W, and T are integers.
- A_{i,j} is one of S, G, ., #, and o.
- Exactly one pair (i,j) satisfies A_{i,j}= S.
- Exactly one pair (i,j) satisfies A_{i,j}= G.
- At most 18 pairs (i,j) satisfy A_{i,j}= o.

Sample Input 1

3 3 5
S.G
o#o
.#.

Sample Output 1

1

If he makes four moves as (1,1) \rightarrow (1,2) \rightarrow (1,3) \rightarrow (2,3) \rightarrow (1,3), he can visit one candy square and finish at the goal square.
He cannot make five or fewer moves to visit two candy squares and finish at the goal square, so the answer is 1.
Note that making five moves as (1,1) \rightarrow (2,1) \rightarrow (1,1) \rightarrow (1,2) \rightarrow (1,3) \rightarrow (2,3) to visit two candy squares is invalid since he would not finish at the goal square.

Sample Input 2

3 3 1
S.G
.#o
o#.

Sample Output 2

-1

He cannot reach the goal square in one or fewer moves.

Sample Input 3

5 10 2000000
S.o..ooo..
..o..o.o..
..o..ooo..
..o..o.o..
..o..ooo.G

Sample Output 3

18

### Solutions
#### Correct
Attempt 1
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    INF = 10**18

    # Locate S, G and candies
    sx = sy = gx = gy = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sx, sy = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gx, gy = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # BFS from each relevant node to compute shortest path lengths to all cells
    # We only need distances among relevant nodes (S, candies, G).
    nodes = [(sx, sy)] + candies + [(gx, gy)]  # size n+2
    m = n + 2

    def bfs(start):
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque([start])
        dist[start[0]][start[1]] = 0
        while q:
            x, y = q.popleft()
            d = dist[x][y]
            for dx, dy in ((1,0), (-1,0), (0,1), (0,-1)):
                nx, ny = x + dx, y + dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and dist[nx][ny] == -1 and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    dist[nx][ny] = d + 1
                    q.append((nx, ny))
        return dist

    dmat = [[INF] * m for _ in range(m)]
    # Compute BFS for each node, extract distances to other nodes
    dists_to_nodes = []
    for k in range(m):
        dist = bfs(nodes[k])
        dists_to_nodes.append(dist)
        for l in range(m):
            x, y = nodes[l]
            dd = dist[x][y]
            if dd != -1:
                dmat[k][l] = dd

    # Quick check reachability to goal within T (without candies)
    if dmat[0][m-1] > T:
        # Still could be possible by visiting candies only if start->goal distance is longer,
        # but shortest path via candies is always >= start->goal direct shortest? Not necessarily.
        # We'll do full DP anyway, so no early return needed.
        pass

    # DP over subsets of candies using TSP-like approach on shortest paths between nodes.
    # dp[mask][i] = minimum moves to start from S (node 0),
    # visit candies in 'mask' (subset of 0..n-1), and end at candy i (0..n-1).
    # Then answer = max popcount(mask) such that min_i dp[mask][i] + dist(candy i -> G) <= T.
    # Also allow visiting no candies: use S->G.
    # Standard bitmask DP: O(2^n * n^2) with n<=18 => ~2^18*324 ~ 85M manageable in Py with optimizations.
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [ [INF]*n for _ in range(size) ]
    # Initialize moves from S to each reachable candy
    for i in range(n):
        d0i = dmat[0][1+i]
        if d0i < INF:
            dp[1<<i][i] = d0i

    # Precompute popcount
    popcnt = [0]*size
    for mask in range(1, size):
        popcnt[mask] = popcnt[mask & (mask-1)] + 1

    best = -1

    # Check case with no candies
    if dmat[0][m-1] <= T:
        best = 0

    # Iterate masks
    for mask in range(size):
        # Prune: if no dp state reachable, skip
        # We'll compute if any dp[mask][i] <= T; but dp values are distances, so still cheap to scan.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Finish by going to goal
            if cur + dmat[1+i][m-1] <= T:
                candies_count = popcnt[mask]
                if candies_count > best:
                    best = candies_count
        # Transition to add a new candy
        # If dp[mask][i] is already INF for all i, transitions won't help; but we don't track that.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Try extend
            nxt_mask_base = (~mask) & (size-1)
            # iterate over remaining bits
            rem = nxt_mask_base
            while rem:
                lb = rem & -rem
                j = (lb.bit_length() - 1)
                rem -= lb
                nd = cur + dmat[1+i][1+j]
                if nd < dp[mask | (1<<j)][j]:
                    if nd <= T:  # optional prune
                        dp[mask | (1<<j)][j] = nd
    # Also consider paths that visit candies but end without candy? Not needed, we always end at some visited candy,
    # then go to G.
    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

Attempt 2
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # All points: 0 = S, 1..n = candies, n+1 = G
    points = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    m = n + 2

    # BFS from each point to compute shortest distances to all cells.
    # Then only keep distances between points; if unreachable, store large.
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * m for _ in range(m)]

    def bfs_from(src_idx):
        r0, c0 = points[src_idx]
        d = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        d[r0][c0] = 0
        q.append((r0, c0))
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            nd = d[r][c] + 1
            for dr, dc in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and d[nr][nc] == -1 and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    d[nr][nc] = nd
                    q.append((nr, nc))
        for j in range(m):
            rj, cj = points[j]
            dj = d[rj][cj]
            if dj != -1:
                dist[src_idx][j] = dj

    for i in range(m):
        bfs_from(i)

    # If goal unreachable at all, answer -1
    if dist[0][m-1] == INF or dist[0][m-1] > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP for max candies with bitmask of visited candies.
    # State: dp[mask][last] = minimum moves to start at S, visit candies in mask,
    # and be at node "last" (where last in 0..n, representing candy index last-1;
    # and last==n means current position is goal? but we keep only candies as last).
    # We'll do classic approach:
    # Let last represent position among candies (0..n-1), plus allow starting at S.
    # Use dp[mask][i] = min moves to be at candy i (i in 0..n-1) after visiting mask (including i).
    # Transition using dist between points.
    # Finally for each dp[mask][i], check if can go to goal within remaining time.
    #
    # Also consider visiting no candies: dist[S][G].
    best = 0
    # candies count = popcount(mask)
    start_to_goal = dist[0][m-1]
    if start_to_goal <= T:
        best = 0

    # If no candies, done
    if n == 0:
        print(best)
        return

    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(size)]

    # init from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        dsi = dist[0][1 + i]
        if dsi != INF and dsi <= T:
            dp[1 << i][i] = dsi

    # iterate masks
    for mask in range(size):
        # small pruning: if mask has some dp value > T ignore when updating
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Try go to next candy
            for nxt in range(n):
                if (mask >> nxt) & 1:
                    continue
                add = dist[1 + last][1 + nxt]
                if add == INF:
                    continue
                nd = cur + add
                if nd <= T:  # only keep those potentially feasible
                    dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt] = min(dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt], nd)

    # evaluate
    for mask in range(size):
        k = mask.bit_count()
        if k <= best:
            continue
        # try finish from any last candy in mask to goal
        for last in range(n):
            if (mask >> last) & 1 == 0:
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            to_goal = dist[1 + last][m - 1]
            if to_goal == INF:
                continue
            if cur + to_goal <= T:
                best = k
                break

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

Attempt 3
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    # Locate S and G, and all candy cells
    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # Precompute shortest distances between S, candies, and G using BFS from each.
    # Nodes: 0 = S, 1..n = candies, n+1 = G  (total n+2 <= 20)
    nodes = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    N = n + 2

    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]

    dirs = [(1, 0), (-1, 0), (0, 1), (0, -1)]

    for a in range(N):
        ar, ac = nodes[a]
        q = deque()
        dmat = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        dmat[ar][ac] = 0
        q.append((ar, ac))
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            for dr, dc in dirs:
                nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and dmat[nr][nc] == -1 and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    dmat[nr][nc] = dmat[r][c] + 1
                    q.append((nr, nc))
        for b in range(N):
            br, bc = nodes[b]
            if dmat[br][bc] != -1:
                dist[a][b] = dmat[br][bc]

    # If S->G unreachable, answer is -1
    if dist[0][n+1] == INF or dist[0][n+1] > T:
        # Could still visit candies and then reach G within T, but if there's no path from S to G at all,
        # then certainly impossible to finish at G.
        # Our DP below already accounts for reaching G, so we can proceed anyway.
        pass

    # DP over subsets:
    # dp[mask][i] = minimum moves to start at S, visit candies in mask, and end at candy i (i in [0..n-1])
    # Only candies are tracked; G is handled at the end.
    # Transitions only among candies.
    # Complexity: O(2^n * n^2) with n<=18 is OK.
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        d = dist[0][i+1]
        if d != INF:
            dp[1 << i][i] = d

    # Fill DP
    for mask in range(size):
        # If mask has no bits, skip (can't be at a candy)
        if mask == 0:
            continue
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Try to go to next candy
            for nxt in range(n):
                bit = 1 << nxt
                if mask & bit:
                    continue
                d = dist[last+1][nxt+1]
                if d == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | bit
                nd = cur + d
                if nd < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = nd

    # Now compute best number of candies that can be visited and then reach G within T.
    # Also consider case of visiting 0 candies: S->G within T.
    ans = -1

    # 0 candies
    if dist[0][n+1] != INF and dist[0][n+1] <= T:
        ans = 0

    # For masks where we end at some candy, check finishing to G
    # Choose maximum popcount among feasible ones.
    # Precompute popcount
    popcnt = [0] * size
    for mask in range(1, size):
        popcnt[mask] = popcnt[mask & (mask - 1)] + 1

    for mask in range(size):
        k = popcnt[mask]
        if k <= ans:
            continue
        # Find if any ending candy last works
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            d_to_g = dist[last+1][n+1]
            if d_to_g == INF:
                continue
            if cur + d_to_g <= T:
                ans = k
                break

    print(ans)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

Attempt 4
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    def idx(r, c):
        return r * W + c

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for r in range(H):
        for c in range(W):
            ch = grid[r][c]
            if ch == 'S':
                sr, sc = r, c
            elif ch == 'G':
                gr, gc = r, c
            elif ch == 'o':
                candies.append((r, c))

    n = len(candies)
    # nodes: 0 = S, 1..n = candies, n+1 = G
    nodes = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    N = n + 2

    # Precompute shortest path distances between all nodes via BFS from each node.
    # Grid size up to 300*300=90000, BFS N times where N<=20 -> ok.
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]

    for sidx, (sr2, sc2) in enumerate(nodes):
        d = [INF] * (H * W)
        q = deque()
        s_id = idx(sr2, sc2)
        d[s_id] = 0
        q.append(s_id)
        while q:
            v = q.popleft()
            vr, vc = divmod(v, W)
            dv = d[v]
            for dr, dc in ((1, 0), (-1, 0), (0, 1), (0, -1)):
                nr, nc = vr + dr, vc + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    ni = idx(nr, nc)
                    if d[ni] > dv + 1:
                        d[ni] = dv + 1
                        q.append(ni)
        for tidx, (tr2, tc2) in enumerate(nodes):
            dist[sidx][tidx] = d[idx(tr2, tc2)]

    # If unreachable from S to G within T, answer -1
    if dist[0][n+1] > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # We need maximum candies visitable with total moves <= T, ending at G.
    # We can model as: start at S, visit subset of candies in some order, end at G.
    # n <= 18 -> DP with bitmask.
    # dp[mask][i] = min moves to start at S, visit candies in mask, and be at candy i (i in [0..n-1])
    # We'll also compute best after reaching some state and then go to G.
    # Use 1D rolling over masks: for each mask we keep array size n.
    # Complexity: O(2^n * n^2) up to 2^18*18^2 ~ 85M, borderline but okay in Python with optimization.
    M = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(M)]
    # initialize from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        dsi = dist[0][i+1]
        if dsi <= T:  # prune
            dp[1 << i][i] = dsi

    best = 0  # maximum candies count feasible

    # If n=0, already checked dist S->G <=T; answer 0.
    if n == 0:
        print(0)
        return

    # Also consider visiting no candies: directly S->G
    best = 0
    for mask in range(M):
        # quick count can be expensive; compute only when checking feasible.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # try go to G
            if cur + dist[i+1][n+1] <= T:
                # count candies in mask
                cnt = mask.bit_count()
                if cnt > best:
                    best = cnt

        # transitions: add next candy j not in mask
        # We'll only do transitions if any state exists.
        # To reduce overhead, iterate i and then j.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # If even going to farthest doesn't help doesn't matter; keep simple
            for j in range(n):
                if (mask >> j) & 1:
                    continue
                nxt = mask | (1 << j)
                nd = cur + dist[i+1][j+1]
                if nd < dp[nxt][j] and nd <= T:
                    dp[nxt][j] = nd

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

Attempt 5
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    si = sj = gi = gj = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                si, sj = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gi, gj = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    K = len(candies)  # <= 18
    nodes = [(si, sj)] + candies + [(gi, gj)]
    N = K + 2  # start + candies + goal

    # BFS from each node to compute shortest paths to all cells.
    # Early stop not necessary; but N <= 20 so it's fine.
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * (H * W) for _ in range(N)]

    def idx(r, c):
        return r * W + c

    dirs = [(1,0), (-1,0), (0,1), (0,-1)]

    for ni, (sr, sc) in enumerate(nodes):
        d = dist[ni]
        q = deque()
        start_idx = idx(sr, sc)
        d[start_idx] = 0
        q.append((sr, sc))
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            curd = d[idx(r, c)]
            nd = curd + 1
            if nd > T + 2:  # small pruning; still safe for reachability comparisons
                # We only need distances relative to T and comparisons.
                pass
            for dr, dc in dirs:
                nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    ni2 = idx(nr, nc)
                    if d[ni2] == INF:
                        d[ni2] = nd
                        q.append((nr, nc))

    # Extract pairwise distances among nodes
    pair = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]
    for a in range(N):
        for b in range(N):
            br, bc = nodes[b]
            pair[a][b] = dist[a][idx(br, bc)]

    # If goal unreachable at all within T from start, answer -1
    start_to_goal = pair[0][N-1]
    if start_to_goal > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets for maximum candies visited with path ending at a given candy
    # Let dp[mask][last] = min distance from start to visit candies in mask and end at candy last
    # We want maximum popcount(mask) such that dp[mask][last] + dist(last->goal) <= T.
    # Nodes for candies are 1..K, goal is N-1.
    M = 1 << K
    dp = [ [INF] * K for _ in range(M) ]

    # Initialize transitions from start to each candy
    for last in range(K):
        d0 = pair[0][last+1]
        if d0 <= T:
            dp[1<<last][last] = d0

    # Transitions
    for mask in range(M):
        for last in range(K):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Optional pruning: if cur > T, no need
            if cur > T:
                continue
            # Try extend to next candy
            for nxt in range(K):
                if mask & (1<<nxt):
                    continue
                nd = cur + pair[last+1][nxt+1]
                if nd <= T + 1_000:  # mild pruning
                    nmask = mask | (1<<nxt)
                    if nd < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                        dp[nmask][nxt] = nd

    # Evaluate best
    best = 0  # can always visit 0 candies if start->goal <= T
    # mask=0 means directly to goal
    # Already ensured reachable within T, so best>=0
    for mask in range(M):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        # check possibility ending at some last
        ok = False
        for last in range(K):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # can we reach goal within T?
            d_goal = pair[last+1][N-1]
            if d_goal == INF:
                continue
            if cur + d_goal <= T:
                ok = True
                break
        if ok and cnt > best:
            best = cnt

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

Attempt 6
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().rstrip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n_c = len(candies)
    # Nodes: candies + start + goal
    N = n_c + 2
    start_id = n_c
    goal_id = n_c + 1

    nodes = candies + [(sr, sc), (gr, gc)]

    # BFS from each node to get shortest distances to all cells
    # Because N <= 20, this is fine.
    dirs = [(1, 0), (-1, 0), (0, 1), (0, -1)]

    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]

    def bfs(src_r, src_c):
        d = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        d[src_r][src_c] = 0
        q.append((src_r, src_c))
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            nd = d[r][c] + 1
            for dr, dc in dirs:
                nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    if d[nr][nc] == -1:
                        d[nr][nc] = nd
                        q.append((nr, nc))
        return d

    # Precompute pairwise distances between relevant nodes
    dmaps = []
    for (r, c) in nodes:
        dmaps.append(bfs(r, c))

    for i in range(N):
        for j in range(N):
            rj, cj = nodes[j]
            dij = dmaps[i][rj][cj]
            dist[i][j] = dij if dij != -1 else INF

    # Quick feasibility: shortest S->G within T?
    s_to_g = dist[start_id][goal_id]
    if s_to_g == INF or s_to_g > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies: Held-Karp for max candies
    # We want maximum number of visited candies (subset) such that
    # min cost from start visiting that subset and ending at some candy,
    # then go to goal within T.
    #
    # Since we only care about visiting each candy at most once (subset),
    # each candy counts once.
    n = n_c
    if n == 0:
        # already feasible checked above
        print(0)
        return

    # Precompute transition costs between candies and start/goal
    # Use indices 0..n-1 for candies
    # cost from i to j: dist[i][j] etc.

    # dp[mask][last] = minimal moves to start at start_id, visit candies in mask, end at last
    # But memory too large for mask up to 2^18 and last up to 18 => 2^18 * 18 ~ 4.7M ok.
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(size)]
    for i in range(n):
        d0 = dist[start_id][i]
        if d0 < INF:
            dp[1 << i][i] = d0

    for mask in range(size):
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # add next
            # If cur > T, no need, but still might become worse; prune
            if cur > T:
                continue
            # try extend
            rem = ((size - 1) ^ mask)
            while rem:
                lsb = rem & -rem
                nxt = (lsb.bit_length() - 1)
                rem -= lsb
                nd = cur + dist[last][nxt]
                if dist[last][nxt] < INF and nd < dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt]:
                    dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt] = nd

    ans = 0
    # Check all subsets: end at some last candy, then go to goal
    # total = dp[mask][last] + dist[last][goal]
    # Also allow mask empty? But start->goal already feasible, ans=0.
    # We'll consider masks with any visited candies.
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= ans:
            continue
        ok = False
        for last in range(n):
            if not (mask & (1 << last)):
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            if cur + dist[last][goal_id] <= T:
                ok = True
                break
        if ok:
            ans = cnt

    print(ans)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

Attempt 7
```python
import sys
import heapq
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    s = g = None
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                s = (i, j)
            elif c == 'G':
                g = (i, j)
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)
    if s is None or g is None:
        print(-1)
        return

    # Map each special node to grid coordinate
    # index: 0 -> S, 1 -> G, 2..n+1 -> candies
    coords = [s, g] + candies
    m = 2 + n

    # For each special node, BFS to get shortest path distances to all cells.
    # We only need distances to other special nodes, but BFS is fine with H,W up to 300.
    INF = 10**18
    dist_to_special = [[INF] * m for _ in range(m)]

    def bfs_from(start_idx):
        si, sj = coords[start_idx]
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        dist[si][sj] = 0
        q.append((si, sj))
        while q:
            i, j = q.popleft()
            d = dist[i][j]
            for di, dj in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                ni, nj = i + di, j + dj
                if 0 <= ni < H and 0 <= nj < W and dist[ni][nj] == -1 and grid[ni][nj] != '#':
                    dist[ni][nj] = d + 1
                    q.append((ni, nj))
        for tj in range(m):
            ti, tjc = coords[tj]
            d = dist[ti][tjc]
            if d != -1:
                dist_to_special[start_idx][tj] = d

    for i in range(m):
        bfs_from(i)

    # If goal unreachable at all, answer is -1
    if dist_to_special[0][1] >= INF or dist_to_special[0][1] > T:
        # still might be possible by visiting candies then reaching goal
        # but if S->G already >T, it's still possible to reach within T using detours? No.
        # Path length only increases with detours, so if S->G > T and any other path must
        # reach G with at least shortest distance S->G, we can still have S->G shortest >T,
        # but a different path could be shorter than S->G shortest? Impossible.
        # Therefore if S->G shortest > T or unreachable, no solution.
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies:
    # dp[mask][i] = min moves to start at S, visit candies in mask, and end at candy i (i in 0..n-1).
    # Then answer from dp[mask][i] + dist(candy i -> G) <= T, maximize |mask|.
    # Classic approach: since n<=18, use bitmask DP.
    full = 1 << n
    dp = [ [INF] * n for _ in range(full) ]

    # Initialize from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        d = dist_to_special[0][2+i]
        if d < INF:
            dp[1<<i][i] = d

    # Transitions
    for mask in range(full):
        # Small pruning: if no states in this mask, skip
        # We'll still check minimal values efficiently by scanning i.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            if cur > T:
                continue
            # try to go to a new candy j
            # We can still update even if >T because final check uses <=T,
            # but pruning helps.
            for j in range(n):
                bit = 1<<j
                if mask & bit:
                    continue
                d = dist_to_special[2+i][2+j]
                if d >= INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | bit
                nd = cur + d
                if nd < dp[nmask][j]:
                    dp[nmask][j] = nd

    # Also consider visiting no candy: just S->G
    best = 0

    # For each mask, check if any end at candy i can reach goal within T
    for mask in range(full):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt < best:
            continue
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            if cur + dist_to_special[2+i][1] <= T:
                best = cnt
                break

    # But need to consider possibility of visiting candies and returning to same candy multiple times:
    # DP already accounts for visiting each candy at least once; shortest route for given order
    # is sufficient because revisits wouldn't help reduce distance.
    # If best not updated but direct S->G within T, it's 0 already.
    # (We earlier returned -1 only if S->G shortest > T.)
    # Ensure best includes possibility of 0 candies:
    if dist_to_special[0][1] <= T:
        best = max(best, 0)

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

Attempt 8
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # Points: start + candies + goal
    points = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    m = n + 2

    # BFS from each point to get shortest distances to all cells
    # and then only keep distances between points.
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF]*m for _ in range(m)]

    dirs = [(1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)]

    for idx, (sx, sy) in enumerate(points):
        d = [[-1]*W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        d[sx][sy] = 0
        q.append((sx, sy))
        while q:
            x, y = q.popleft()
            for dx, dy in dirs:
                nx, ny = x+dx, y+dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    if d[nx][ny] == -1:
                        d[nx][ny] = d[x][y] + 1
                        q.append((nx, ny))
        for jdx, (tx, ty) in enumerate(points):
            val = d[tx][ty]
            if val != -1:
                dist[idx][jdx] = val

    # Check feasibility from start to goal
    start_to_goal = dist[0][m-1]
    if start_to_goal == INF or start_to_goal > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # Held-Karp DP for visiting subset of candies, ending at some point among candies
    # dp[mask][i] = min moves starting from start, visiting candies in mask,
    # ending at candy i (i in [0..n-1]).
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF]*n for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize with transitions from start to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        if dist[0][1+i] != INF:
            dp[1<<i][i] = dist[0][1+i]

    # Precompute for faster iteration: for each mask, list bits? We'll do standard loops with pruning.
    for mask in range(size):
        # For each end candy i in mask
        # We'll iterate over i and check if bit set.
        for i in range(n):
            if not (mask >> i) & 1:
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Transition to add another candy j
            # (if exists)
            rem = (~mask) & (size-1)
            while rem:
                lsb = rem & -rem
                j = (lsb.bit_length() - 1)
                rem -= lsb
                d_ij = dist[1+i][1+j]
                if d_ij == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1<<j)
                nd = cur + d_ij
                if nd < dp[nmask][j]:
                    dp[nmask][j] = nd

    # Now compute best candies count with total distance <= T:
    # total = dp[mask][i] + dist[candy i][goal]
    best = 0
    # Also consider visiting none: just start->goal
    best = 0

    goal_idx = m - 1
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= best:
            continue
        # if can end at some candy i in mask within T
        ok = False
        for i in range(n):
            if (mask >> i) & 1:
                if dp[mask][i] == INF:
                    continue
                to_goal = dist[1+i][goal_idx]
                if to_goal == INF:
                    continue
                if dp[mask][i] + to_goal <= T:
                    ok = True
                    break
        if ok:
            best = cnt

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

Attempt 9
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    # Locate start, goal, candies
    candies = []
    sx = sy = gx = gy = -1
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sx, sy = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gx, gy = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n_c = len(candies)  # <= 18

    def bfs_from(start):
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque([start])
        dist[start[0]][start[1]] = 0
        while q:
            x, y = q.popleft()
            d = dist[x][y]
            nd = d + 1
            if nd > T:  # no need beyond T for reachability/speed
                continue
            for dx, dy in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                nx, ny = x + dx, y + dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    if dist[nx][ny] == -1:
                        dist[nx][ny] = nd
                        q.append((nx, ny))
        return dist

    # Compute pairwise shortest path lengths among {S, candies..., G}
    points = [(sx, sy)] + candies + [(gx, gy)]
    m = 1 + n_c + 1  # number of points
    dmat = [[10**18] * m for _ in range(m)]

    for i in range(m):
        dist = bfs_from(points[i])
        xi, yi = points[i]
        # fill distances from i to others
        for j in range(m):
            xj, yj = points[j]
            dij = dist[xj][yj]
            if dij != -1:
                dmat[i][j] = dij

    # If cannot reach goal directly
    if dmat[0][m-1] > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies:
    # nodes 1..n_c correspond to candies
    # We'll do DP[mask][i] = min moves to start at S, visit candies in mask, end at candy i (i is index in 0..n_c-1)
    # Use bitmask DP with n_c <= 18 (2^18 * 18 about 4.7M)
    INF = 10**18
    size = 1 << n_c
    dp = [[INF] * n_c for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize: from S to each candy
    for i in range(n_c):
        t = dmat[0][1 + i]
        if t <= T:
            dp[1 << i][i] = t

    # Transition
    # For speed: iterate masks, try extend to new candy
    for mask in range(size):
        # quick check if mask has any reachable end
        for last in range(n_c):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # extend
            for nxt in range(n_c):
                if (mask >> nxt) & 1:
                    continue
                w = dmat[1 + last][1 + nxt]
                if w == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1 << nxt)
                nd = cur + w
                if nd <= T and nd < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = nd

    # Evaluate best number of candies for masks (possibly empty mask as well)
    # Need end at goal within T moves.
    # Consider:
    # - empty set: S->G
    ans = 0
    best_found = False
    if dmat[0][m-1] <= T:
        ans = 0
        best_found = True

    # For each mask and last candy: go from last candy to goal
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        for last in range(n_c):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            w = dmat[1 + last][m-1]
            if w == INF:
                continue
            if cur + w <= T:
                if not best_found or cnt > ans:
                    ans = cnt
                    best_found = True

    print(ans if best_found else -1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

#### Partially Correct
Attempt 1
```python
import sys
import heapq

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sx = sy = gx = gy = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sx, sy = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gx, gy = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    C = len(candies)
    # If no candies, just check reachability within T
    # (Still handled by DP, but keep fast fail)
    INF = 10**18

    # Build mapping from important nodes: start=0, candies=1..C, goal=C+1
    n = C + 2
    pos = [(sx, sy)] + candies + [(gx, gy)]

    # Precompute shortest path distances between all important nodes
    # using BFS on unweighted grid (walls are blocked)
    def bfs_from(src_i):
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        si, sj = pos[src_i]
        q = [(si, sj)]
        dist[si][sj] = 0
        head = 0
        while head < len(q):
            x, y = q[head]
            head += 1
            nd = dist[x][y] + 1
            if x > 0 and dist[x-1][y] == -1 and grid[x-1][y] != '#':
                dist[x-1][y] = nd
                q.append((x-1, y))
            if x + 1 < H and dist[x+1][y] == -1 and grid[x+1][y] != '#':
                dist[x+1][y] = nd
                q.append((x+1, y))
            if y > 0 and dist[x][y-1] == -1 and grid[x][y-1] != '#':
                dist[x][y-1] = nd
                q.append((x, y-1))
            if y + 1 < W and dist[x][y+1] == -1 and grid[x][y+1] != '#':
                dist[x][y+1] = nd
                q.append((x, y+1))
        dists = []
        for k in range(n):
            x, y = pos[k]
            d = dist[x][y]
            dists.append(d)
        return dists

    d = []
    for i in range(n):
        d.append(bfs_from(i))

    # If goal unreachable from start at all
    if d[0][n-1] == -1:
        print(-1)
        return

    # Now solve: maximize number of candies visited with path length <= T
    # Start at node 0, must end at goal node n-1.
    # Moves cost = shortest path distances between nodes.
    #
    # Because candies <= 18, use bitmask DP traveling among candies.
    # Standard "collect subset" DP: dp[mask][last] = min cost to start at 0,
    # visit candies in mask, and end at candy 'last' (last is index 0..C-1).
    #
    # Then total cost = dp[mask][last] + dist(last->goal).
    # Also possibility of visiting empty subset: start->goal directly.
    #
    # If there are disconnected distances, ignore transitions.
    full_mask = 1 << C
    # Use large array: dp[mask][last] for last in 0..C-1
    # Size: up to 2^18 * 18 ~ 4.7M, feasible.
    dp = [[INF] * C for _ in range(full_mask)]

    # init: visit single candy k
    for k in range(C):
        dist_start = d[0][1 + k]
        if dist_start != -1:
            dp[1 << k][k] = dist_start

    best = 0
    # empty subset
    if d[0][n-1] != -1 and d[0][n-1] <= T:
        best = 0

    # iterate masks
    for mask in range(full_mask):
        # pruning: if mask has no bits, already checked
        # We'll attempt to compute best using any last; no easy pruning for dp.
        # Transition
        # For each last included
        for last in range(C):
            if not (mask >> last) & 1:
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Finish to goal
            to_goal = d[1 + last][n-1]
            if to_goal != -1:
                total = cur + to_goal
                if total <= T:
                    cnt = mask.bit_count()
                    if cnt > best:
                        best = cnt
            # extend to new candy
            # next bits
            rem = (~mask) & (full_mask - 1)
            while rem:
                nxt = (rem & -rem).bit_length() - 1
                rem -= (1 << nxt)
                dist_last_to_nxt = d[1 + last][1 + nxt]
                if dist_last_to_nxt == -1:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1 << nxt)
                val = cur + dist_last_to_nxt
                if val < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = val

    # Additionally, in case of visiting candies but with redundant possibility:
    # DP already handles ending at goal after last candy.
    # If goal is reachable without candies, best already set to 0.
    # If cannot reach goal at all -> handled above.
    if best == 0:
        # Could be that only empty subset is feasible, then best=0 is fine.
        # But if unreachable overall, already returned -1.
        pass
    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

<summary>full attempt 1</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    INF = 10**18

    # Locate S, G and candies
    sx = sy = gx = gy = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sx, sy = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gx, gy = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # BFS from each relevant node to compute shortest path lengths to all cells
    # We only need distances among relevant nodes (S, candies, G).
    nodes = [(sx, sy)] + candies + [(gx, gy)]  # size n+2
    m = n + 2

    def bfs(start):
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque([start])
        dist[start[0]][start[1]] = 0
        while q:
            x, y = q.popleft()
            d = dist[x][y]
            for dx, dy in ((1,0), (-1,0), (0,1), (0,-1)):
                nx, ny = x + dx, y + dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and dist[nx][ny] == -1 and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    dist[nx][ny] = d + 1
                    q.append((nx, ny))
        return dist

    dmat = [[INF] * m for _ in range(m)]
    # Compute BFS for each node, extract distances to other nodes
    dists_to_nodes = []
    for k in range(m):
        dist = bfs(nodes[k])
        dists_to_nodes.append(dist)
        for l in range(m):
            x, y = nodes[l]
            dd = dist[x][y]
            if dd != -1:
                dmat[k][l] = dd

    # Quick check reachability to goal within T (without candies)
    if dmat[0][m-1] > T:
        # Still could be possible by visiting candies only if start->goal distance is longer,
        # but shortest path via candies is always >= start->goal direct shortest? Not necessarily.
        # We'll do full DP anyway, so no early return needed.
        pass

    # DP over subsets of candies using TSP-like approach on shortest paths between nodes.
    # dp[mask][i] = minimum moves to start from S (node 0),
    # visit candies in 'mask' (subset of 0..n-1), and end at candy i (0..n-1).
    # Then answer = max popcount(mask) such that min_i dp[mask][i] + dist(candy i -> G) <= T.
    # Also allow visiting no candies: use S->G.
    # Standard bitmask DP: O(2^n * n^2) with n<=18 => ~2^18*324 ~ 85M manageable in Py with optimizations.
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [ [INF]*n for _ in range(size) ]
    # Initialize moves from S to each reachable candy
    for i in range(n):
        d0i = dmat[0][1+i]
        if d0i < INF:
            dp[1<<i][i] = d0i

    # Precompute popcount
    popcnt = [0]*size
    for mask in range(1, size):
        popcnt[mask] = popcnt[mask & (mask-1)] + 1

    best = -1

    # Check case with no candies
    if dmat[0][m-1] <= T:
        best = 0

    # Iterate masks
    for mask in range(size):
        # Prune: if no dp state reachable, skip
        # We'll compute if any dp[mask][i] <= T; but dp values are distances, so still cheap to scan.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Finish by going to goal
            if cur + dmat[1+i][m-1] <= T:
                candies_count = popcnt[mask]
                if candies_count > best:
                    best = candies_count
        # Transition to add a new candy
        # If dp[mask][i] is already INF for all i, transitions won't help; but we don't track that.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Try extend
            nxt_mask_base = (~mask) & (size-1)
            # iterate over remaining bits
            rem = nxt_mask_base
            while rem:
                lb = rem & -rem
                j = (lb.bit_length() - 1)
                rem -= lb
                nd = cur + dmat[1+i][1+j]
                if nd < dp[mask | (1<<j)][j]:
                    if nd <= T:  # optional prune
                        dp[mask | (1<<j)][j] = nd
    # Also consider paths that visit candies but end without candy? Not needed, we always end at some visited candy,
    # then go to G.
    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()

```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # All points: 0 = S, 1..n = candies, n+1 = G
    points = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    m = n + 2

    # BFS from each point to compute shortest distances to all cells.
    # Then only keep distances between points; if unreachable, store large.
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * m for _ in range(m)]

    def bfs_from(src_idx):
        r0, c0 = points[src_idx]
        d = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        d[r0][c0] = 0
        q.append((r0, c0))
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            nd = d[r][c] + 1
            for dr, dc in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and d[nr][nc] == -1 and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    d[nr][nc] = nd
                    q.append((nr, nc))
        for j in range(m):
            rj, cj = points[j]
            dj = d[rj][cj]
            if dj != -1:
                dist[src_idx][j] = dj

    for i in range(m):
        bfs_from(i)

    # If goal unreachable at all, answer -1
    if dist[0][m-1] == INF or dist[0][m-1] > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP for max candies with bitmask of visited candies.
    # State: dp[mask][last] = minimum moves to start at S, visit candies in mask,
    # and be at node "last" (where last in 0..n, representing candy index last-1;
    # and last==n means current position is goal? but we keep only candies as last).
    # We'll do classic approach:
    # Let last represent position among candies (0..n-1), plus allow starting at S.
    # Use dp[mask][i] = min moves to be at candy i (i in 0..n-1) after visiting mask (including i).
    # Transition using dist between points.
    # Finally for each dp[mask][i], check if can go to goal within remaining time.
    #
    # Also consider visiting no candies: dist[S][G].
    best = 0
    # candies count = popcount(mask)
    start_to_goal = dist[0][m-1]
    if start_to_goal <= T:
        best = 0

    # If no candies, done
    if n == 0:
        print(best)
        return

    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(size)]

    # init from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        dsi = dist[0][1 + i]
        if dsi != INF and dsi <= T:
            dp[1 << i][i] = dsi

    # iterate masks
    for mask in range(size):
        # small pruning: if mask has some dp value > T ignore when updating
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Try go to next candy
            for nxt in range(n):
                if (mask >> nxt) & 1:
                    continue
                add = dist[1 + last][1 + nxt]
                if add == INF:
                    continue
                nd = cur + add
                if nd <= T:  # only keep those potentially feasible
                    dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt] = min(dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt], nd)

    # evaluate
    for mask in range(size):
        k = mask.bit_count()
        if k <= best:
            continue
        # try finish from any last candy in mask to goal
        for last in range(n):
            if (mask >> last) & 1 == 0:
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            to_goal = dist[1 + last][m - 1]
            if to_goal == INF:
                continue
            if cur + to_goal <= T:
                best = k
                break

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    # Locate S and G, and all candy cells
    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # Precompute shortest distances between S, candies, and G using BFS from each.
    # Nodes: 0 = S, 1..n = candies, n+1 = G  (total n+2 <= 20)
    nodes = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    N = n + 2

    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]

    dirs = [(1, 0), (-1, 0), (0, 1), (0, -1)]

    for a in range(N):
        ar, ac = nodes[a]
        q = deque()
        dmat = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        dmat[ar][ac] = 0
        q.append((ar, ac))
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            for dr, dc in dirs:
                nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and dmat[nr][nc] == -1 and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    dmat[nr][nc] = dmat[r][c] + 1
                    q.append((nr, nc))
        for b in range(N):
            br, bc = nodes[b]
            if dmat[br][bc] != -1:
                dist[a][b] = dmat[br][bc]

    # If S->G unreachable, answer is -1
    if dist[0][n+1] == INF or dist[0][n+1] > T:
        # Could still visit candies and then reach G within T, but if there's no path from S to G at all,
        # then certainly impossible to finish at G.
        # Our DP below already accounts for reaching G, so we can proceed anyway.
        pass

    # DP over subsets:
    # dp[mask][i] = minimum moves to start at S, visit candies in mask, and end at candy i (i in [0..n-1])
    # Only candies are tracked; G is handled at the end.
    # Transitions only among candies.
    # Complexity: O(2^n * n^2) with n<=18 is OK.
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        d = dist[0][i+1]
        if d != INF:
            dp[1 << i][i] = d

    # Fill DP
    for mask in range(size):
        # If mask has no bits, skip (can't be at a candy)
        if mask == 0:
            continue
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Try to go to next candy
            for nxt in range(n):
                bit = 1 << nxt
                if mask & bit:
                    continue
                d = dist[last+1][nxt+1]
                if d == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | bit
                nd = cur + d
                if nd < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = nd

    # Now compute best number of candies that can be visited and then reach G within T.
    # Also consider case of visiting 0 candies: S->G within T.
    ans = -1

    # 0 candies
    if dist[0][n+1] != INF and dist[0][n+1] <= T:
        ans = 0

    # For masks where we end at some candy, check finishing to G
    # Choose maximum popcount among feasible ones.
    # Precompute popcount
    popcnt = [0] * size
    for mask in range(1, size):
        popcnt[mask] = popcnt[mask & (mask - 1)] + 1

    for mask in range(size):
        k = popcnt[mask]
        if k <= ans:
            continue
        # Find if any ending candy last works
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            d_to_g = dist[last+1][n+1]
            if d_to_g == INF:
                continue
            if cur + d_to_g <= T:
                ans = k
                break

    print(ans)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    def idx(r, c):
        return r * W + c

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for r in range(H):
        for c in range(W):
            ch = grid[r][c]
            if ch == 'S':
                sr, sc = r, c
            elif ch == 'G':
                gr, gc = r, c
            elif ch == 'o':
                candies.append((r, c))

    n = len(candies)
    # nodes: 0 = S, 1..n = candies, n+1 = G
    nodes = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    N = n + 2

    # Precompute shortest path distances between all nodes via BFS from each node.
    # Grid size up to 300*300=90000, BFS N times where N<=20 -> ok.
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]

    for sidx, (sr2, sc2) in enumerate(nodes):
        d = [INF] * (H * W)
        q = deque()
        s_id = idx(sr2, sc2)
        d[s_id] = 0
        q.append(s_id)
        while q:
            v = q.popleft()
            vr, vc = divmod(v, W)
            dv = d[v]
            for dr, dc in ((1, 0), (-1, 0), (0, 1), (0, -1)):
                nr, nc = vr + dr, vc + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    ni = idx(nr, nc)
                    if d[ni] > dv + 1:
                        d[ni] = dv + 1
                        q.append(ni)
        for tidx, (tr2, tc2) in enumerate(nodes):
            dist[sidx][tidx] = d[idx(tr2, tc2)]

    # If unreachable from S to G within T, answer -1
    if dist[0][n+1] > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # We need maximum candies visitable with total moves <= T, ending at G.
    # We can model as: start at S, visit subset of candies in some order, end at G.
    # n <= 18 -> DP with bitmask.
    # dp[mask][i] = min moves to start at S, visit candies in mask, and be at candy i (i in [0..n-1])
    # We'll also compute best after reaching some state and then go to G.
    # Use 1D rolling over masks: for each mask we keep array size n.
    # Complexity: O(2^n * n^2) up to 2^18*18^2 ~ 85M, borderline but okay in Python with optimization.
    M = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(M)]
    # initialize from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        dsi = dist[0][i+1]
        if dsi <= T:  # prune
            dp[1 << i][i] = dsi

    best = 0  # maximum candies count feasible

    # If n=0, already checked dist S->G <=T; answer 0.
    if n == 0:
        print(0)
        return

    # Also consider visiting no candies: directly S->G
    best = 0
    for mask in range(M):
        # quick count can be expensive; compute only when checking feasible.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # try go to G
            if cur + dist[i+1][n+1] <= T:
                # count candies in mask
                cnt = mask.bit_count()
                if cnt > best:
                    best = cnt

        # transitions: add next candy j not in mask
        # We'll only do transitions if any state exists.
        # To reduce overhead, iterate i and then j.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # If even going to farthest doesn't help doesn't matter; keep simple
            for j in range(n):
                if (mask >> j) & 1:
                    continue
                nxt = mask | (1 << j)
                nd = cur + dist[i+1][j+1]
                if nd < dp[nxt][j] and nd <= T:
                    dp[nxt][j] = nd

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    si = sj = gi = gj = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                si, sj = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gi, gj = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    K = len(candies)  # <= 18
    nodes = [(si, sj)] + candies + [(gi, gj)]
    N = K + 2  # start + candies + goal

    # BFS from each node to compute shortest paths to all cells.
    # Early stop not necessary; but N <= 20 so it's fine.
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * (H * W) for _ in range(N)]

    def idx(r, c):
        return r * W + c

    dirs = [(1,0), (-1,0), (0,1), (0,-1)]

    for ni, (sr, sc) in enumerate(nodes):
        d = dist[ni]
        q = deque()
        start_idx = idx(sr, sc)
        d[start_idx] = 0
        q.append((sr, sc))
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            curd = d[idx(r, c)]
            nd = curd + 1
            if nd > T + 2:  # small pruning; still safe for reachability comparisons
                # We only need distances relative to T and comparisons.
                pass
            for dr, dc in dirs:
                nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    ni2 = idx(nr, nc)
                    if d[ni2] == INF:
                        d[ni2] = nd
                        q.append((nr, nc))

    # Extract pairwise distances among nodes
    pair = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]
    for a in range(N):
        for b in range(N):
            br, bc = nodes[b]
            pair[a][b] = dist[a][idx(br, bc)]

    # If goal unreachable at all within T from start, answer -1
    start_to_goal = pair[0][N-1]
    if start_to_goal > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets for maximum candies visited with path ending at a given candy
    # Let dp[mask][last] = min distance from start to visit candies in mask and end at candy last
    # We want maximum popcount(mask) such that dp[mask][last] + dist(last->goal) <= T.
    # Nodes for candies are 1..K, goal is N-1.
    M = 1 << K
    dp = [ [INF] * K for _ in range(M) ]

    # Initialize transitions from start to each candy
    for last in range(K):
        d0 = pair[0][last+1]
        if d0 <= T:
            dp[1<<last][last] = d0

    # Transitions
    for mask in range(M):
        for last in range(K):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Optional pruning: if cur > T, no need
            if cur > T:
                continue
            # Try extend to next candy
            for nxt in range(K):
                if mask & (1<<nxt):
                    continue
                nd = cur + pair[last+1][nxt+1]
                if nd <= T + 1_000:  # mild pruning
                    nmask = mask | (1<<nxt)
                    if nd < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                        dp[nmask][nxt] = nd

    # Evaluate best
    best = 0  # can always visit 0 candies if start->goal <= T
    # mask=0 means directly to goal
    # Already ensured reachable within T, so best>=0
    for mask in range(M):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        # check possibility ending at some last
        ok = False
        for last in range(K):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # can we reach goal within T?
            d_goal = pair[last+1][N-1]
            if d_goal == INF:
                continue
            if cur + d_goal <= T:
                ok = True
                break
        if ok and cnt > best:
            best = cnt

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().rstrip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n_c = len(candies)
    # Nodes: candies + start + goal
    N = n_c + 2
    start_id = n_c
    goal_id = n_c + 1

    nodes = candies + [(sr, sc), (gr, gc)]

    # BFS from each node to get shortest distances to all cells
    # Because N <= 20, this is fine.
    dirs = [(1, 0), (-1, 0), (0, 1), (0, -1)]

    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]

    def bfs(src_r, src_c):
        d = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        d[src_r][src_c] = 0
        q.append((src_r, src_c))
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            nd = d[r][c] + 1
            for dr, dc in dirs:
                nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    if d[nr][nc] == -1:
                        d[nr][nc] = nd
                        q.append((nr, nc))
        return d

    # Precompute pairwise distances between relevant nodes
    dmaps = []
    for (r, c) in nodes:
        dmaps.append(bfs(r, c))

    for i in range(N):
        for j in range(N):
            rj, cj = nodes[j]
            dij = dmaps[i][rj][cj]
            dist[i][j] = dij if dij != -1 else INF

    # Quick feasibility: shortest S->G within T?
    s_to_g = dist[start_id][goal_id]
    if s_to_g == INF or s_to_g > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies: Held-Karp for max candies
    # We want maximum number of visited candies (subset) such that
    # min cost from start visiting that subset and ending at some candy,
    # then go to goal within T.
    #
    # Since we only care about visiting each candy at most once (subset),
    # each candy counts once.
    n = n_c
    if n == 0:
        # already feasible checked above
        print(0)
        return

    # Precompute transition costs between candies and start/goal
    # Use indices 0..n-1 for candies
    # cost from i to j: dist[i][j] etc.

    # dp[mask][last] = minimal moves to start at start_id, visit candies in mask, end at last
    # But memory too large for mask up to 2^18 and last up to 18 => 2^18 * 18 ~ 4.7M ok.
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(size)]
    for i in range(n):
        d0 = dist[start_id][i]
        if d0 < INF:
            dp[1 << i][i] = d0

    for mask in range(size):
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # add next
            # If cur > T, no need, but still might become worse; prune
            if cur > T:
                continue
            # try extend
            rem = ((size - 1) ^ mask)
            while rem:
                lsb = rem & -rem
                nxt = (lsb.bit_length() - 1)
                rem -= lsb
                nd = cur + dist[last][nxt]
                if dist[last][nxt] < INF and nd < dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt]:
                    dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt] = nd

    ans = 0
    # Check all subsets: end at some last candy, then go to goal
    # total = dp[mask][last] + dist[last][goal]
    # Also allow mask empty? But start->goal already feasible, ans=0.
    # We'll consider masks with any visited candies.
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= ans:
            continue
        ok = False
        for last in range(n):
            if not (mask & (1 << last)):
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            if cur + dist[last][goal_id] <= T:
                ok = True
                break
        if ok:
            ans = cnt

    print(ans)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

```text
```python
import sys
import heapq
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    s = g = None
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                s = (i, j)
            elif c == 'G':
                g = (i, j)
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)
    if s is None or g is None:
        print(-1)
        return

    # Map each special node to grid coordinate
    # index: 0 -> S, 1 -> G, 2..n+1 -> candies
    coords = [s, g] + candies
    m = 2 + n

    # For each special node, BFS to get shortest path distances to all cells.
    # We only need distances to other special nodes, but BFS is fine with H,W up to 300.
    INF = 10**18
    dist_to_special = [[INF] * m for _ in range(m)]

    def bfs_from(start_idx):
        si, sj = coords[start_idx]
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        dist[si][sj] = 0
        q.append((si, sj))
        while q:
            i, j = q.popleft()
            d = dist[i][j]
            for di, dj in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                ni, nj = i + di, j + dj
                if 0 <= ni < H and 0 <= nj < W and dist[ni][nj] == -1 and grid[ni][nj] != '#':
                    dist[ni][nj] = d + 1
                    q.append((ni, nj))
        for tj in range(m):
            ti, tjc = coords[tj]
            d = dist[ti][tjc]
            if d != -1:
                dist_to_special[start_idx][tj] = d

    for i in range(m):
        bfs_from(i)

    # If goal unreachable at all, answer is -1
    if dist_to_special[0][1] >= INF or dist_to_special[0][1] > T:
        # still might be possible by visiting candies then reaching goal
        # but if S->G already >T, it's still possible to reach within T using detours? No.
        # Path length only increases with detours, so if S->G > T and any other path must
        # reach G with at least shortest distance S->G, we can still have S->G shortest >T,
        # but a different path could be shorter than S->G shortest? Impossible.
        # Therefore if S->G shortest > T or unreachable, no solution.
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies:
    # dp[mask][i] = min moves to start at S, visit candies in mask, and end at candy i (i in 0..n-1).
    # Then answer from dp[mask][i] + dist(candy i -> G) <= T, maximize |mask|.
    # Classic approach: since n<=18, use bitmask DP.
    full = 1 << n
    dp = [ [INF] * n for _ in range(full) ]

    # Initialize from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        d = dist_to_special[0][2+i]
        if d < INF:
            dp[1<<i][i] = d

    # Transitions
    for mask in range(full):
        # Small pruning: if no states in this mask, skip
        # We'll still check minimal values efficiently by scanning i.
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            if cur > T:
                continue
            # try to go to a new candy j
            # We can still update even if >T because final check uses <=T,
            # but pruning helps.
            for j in range(n):
                bit = 1<<j
                if mask & bit:
                    continue
                d = dist_to_special[2+i][2+j]
                if d >= INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | bit
                nd = cur + d
                if nd < dp[nmask][j]:
                    dp[nmask][j] = nd

    # Also consider visiting no candy: just S->G
    best = 0

    # For each mask, check if any end at candy i can reach goal within T
    for mask in range(full):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt < best:
            continue
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            if cur + dist_to_special[2+i][1] <= T:
                best = cnt
                break

    # But need to consider possibility of visiting candies and returning to same candy multiple times:
    # DP already accounts for visiting each candy at least once; shortest route for given order
    # is sufficient because revisits wouldn't help reduce distance.
    # If best not updated but direct S->G within T, it's 0 already.
    # (We earlier returned -1 only if S->G shortest > T.)
    # Ensure best includes possibility of 0 candies:
    if dist_to_special[0][1] <= T:
        best = max(best, 0)

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # Points: start + candies + goal
    points = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    m = n + 2

    # BFS from each point to get shortest distances to all cells
    # and then only keep distances between points.
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF]*m for _ in range(m)]

    dirs = [(1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)]

    for idx, (sx, sy) in enumerate(points):
        d = [[-1]*W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        d[sx][sy] = 0
        q.append((sx, sy))
        while q:
            x, y = q.popleft()
            for dx, dy in dirs:
                nx, ny = x+dx, y+dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    if d[nx][ny] == -1:
                        d[nx][ny] = d[x][y] + 1
                        q.append((nx, ny))
        for jdx, (tx, ty) in enumerate(points):
            val = d[tx][ty]
            if val != -1:
                dist[idx][jdx] = val

    # Check feasibility from start to goal
    start_to_goal = dist[0][m-1]
    if start_to_goal == INF or start_to_goal > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # Held-Karp DP for visiting subset of candies, ending at some point among candies
    # dp[mask][i] = min moves starting from start, visiting candies in mask,
    # ending at candy i (i in [0..n-1]).
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF]*n for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize with transitions from start to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        if dist[0][1+i] != INF:
            dp[1<<i][i] = dist[0][1+i]

    # Precompute for faster iteration: for each mask, list bits? We'll do standard loops with pruning.
    for mask in range(size):
        # For each end candy i in mask
        # We'll iterate over i and check if bit set.
        for i in range(n):
            if not (mask >> i) & 1:
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Transition to add another candy j
            # (if exists)
            rem = (~mask) & (size-1)
            while rem:
                lsb = rem & -rem
                j = (lsb.bit_length() - 1)
                rem -= lsb
                d_ij = dist[1+i][1+j]
                if d_ij == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1<<j)
                nd = cur + d_ij
                if nd < dp[nmask][j]:
                    dp[nmask][j] = nd

    # Now compute best candies count with total distance <= T:
    # total = dp[mask][i] + dist[candy i][goal]
    best = 0
    # Also consider visiting none: just start->goal
    best = 0

    goal_idx = m - 1
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= best:
            continue
        # if can end at some candy i in mask within T
        ok = False
        for i in range(n):
            if (mask >> i) & 1:
                if dp[mask][i] == INF:
                    continue
                to_goal = dist[1+i][goal_idx]
                if to_goal == INF:
                    continue
                if dp[mask][i] + to_goal <= T:
                    ok = True
                    break
        if ok:
            best = cnt

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```
