<summary>full attempt 9</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    # Locate start, goal, candies
    candies = []
    sx = sy = gx = gy = -1
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sx, sy = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gx, gy = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n_c = len(candies)  # <= 18

    def bfs_from(start):
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque([start])
        dist[start[0]][start[1]] = 0
        while q:
            x, y = q.popleft()
            d = dist[x][y]
            nd = d + 1
            if nd > T:  # no need beyond T for reachability/speed
                continue
            for dx, dy in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                nx, ny = x + dx, y + dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    if dist[nx][ny] == -1:
                        dist[nx][ny] = nd
                        q.append((nx, ny))
        return dist

    # Compute pairwise shortest path lengths among {S, candies..., G}
    points = [(sx, sy)] + candies + [(gx, gy)]
    m = 1 + n_c + 1  # number of points
    dmat = [[10**18] * m for _ in range(m)]

    for i in range(m):
        dist = bfs_from(points[i])
        xi, yi = points[i]
        # fill distances from i to others
        for j in range(m):
            xj, yj = points[j]
            dij = dist[xj][yj]
            if dij != -1:
                dmat[i][j] = dij

    # If cannot reach goal directly
    if dmat[0][m-1] > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies:
    # nodes 1..n_c correspond to candies
    # We'll do DP[mask][i] = min moves to start at S, visit candies in mask, end at candy i (i is index in 0..n_c-1)
    # Use bitmask DP with n_c <= 18 (2^18 * 18 about 4.7M)
    INF = 10**18
    size = 1 << n_c
    dp = [[INF] * n_c for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize: from S to each candy
    for i in range(n_c):
        t = dmat[0][1 + i]
        if t <= T:
            dp[1 << i][i] = t

    # Transition
    # For speed: iterate masks, try extend to new candy
    for mask in range(size):
        # quick check if mask has any reachable end
        for last in range(n_c):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # extend
            for nxt in range(n_c):
                if (mask >> nxt) & 1:
                    continue
                w = dmat[1 + last][1 + nxt]
                if w == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1 << nxt)
                nd = cur + w
                if nd <= T and nd < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = nd

    # Evaluate best number of candies for masks (possibly empty mask as well)
    # Need end at goal within T moves.
    # Consider:
    # - empty set: S->G
    ans = 0
    best_found = False
    if dmat[0][m-1] <= T:
        ans = 0
        best_found = True

    # For each mask and last candy: go from last candy to goal
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        for last in range(n_c):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            w = dmat[1 + last][m-1]
            if w == INF:
                continue
            if cur + w <= T:
                if not best_found or cnt > ans:
                    ans = cnt
                    best_found = True

    print(ans if best_found else -1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

```text
```python
import sys
import heapq

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sx = sy = gx = gy = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sx, sy = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gx, gy = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    C = len(candies)
    # If no candies, just check reachability within T
    # (Still handled by DP, but keep fast fail)
    INF = 10**18

    # Build mapping from important nodes: start=0, candies=1..C, goal=C+1
    n = C + 2
    pos = [(sx, sy)] + candies + [(gx, gy)]

    # Precompute shortest path distances between all important nodes
    # using BFS on unweighted grid (walls are blocked)
    def bfs_from(src_i):
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        si, sj = pos[src_i]
        q = [(si, sj)]
        dist[si][sj] = 0
        head = 0
        while head < len(q):
            x, y = q[head]
            head += 1
            nd = dist[x][y] + 1
            if x > 0 and dist[x-1][y] == -1 and grid[x-1][y] != '#':
                dist[x-1][y] = nd
                q.append((x-1, y))
            if x + 1 < H and dist[x+1][y] == -1 and grid[x+1][y] != '#':
                dist[x+1][y] = nd
                q.append((x+1, y))
            if y > 0 and dist[x][y-1] == -1 and grid[x][y-1] != '#':
                dist[x][y-1] = nd
                q.append((x, y-1))
            if y + 1 < W and dist[x][y+1] == -1 and grid[x][y+1] != '#':
                dist[x][y+1] = nd
                q.append((x, y+1))
        dists = []
        for k in range(n):
            x, y = pos[k]
            d = dist[x][y]
            dists.append(d)
        return dists

    d = []
    for i in range(n):
        d.append(bfs_from(i))

    # If goal unreachable from start at all
    if d[0][n-1] == -1:
        print(-1)
        return

    # Now solve: maximize number of candies visited with path length <= T
    # Start at node 0, must end at goal node n-1.
    # Moves cost = shortest path distances between nodes.
    #
    # Because candies <= 18, use bitmask DP traveling among candies.
    # Standard "collect subset" DP: dp[mask][last] = min cost to start at 0,
    # visit candies in mask, and end at candy 'last' (last is index 0..C-1).
    #
    # Then total cost = dp[mask][last] + dist(last->goal).
    # Also possibility of visiting empty subset: start->goal directly.
    #
    # If there are disconnected distances, ignore transitions.
    full_mask = 1 << C
    # Use large array: dp[mask][last] for last in 0..C-1
    # Size: up to 2^18 * 18 ~ 4.7M, feasible.
    dp = [[INF] * C for _ in range(full_mask)]

    # init: visit single candy k
    for k in range(C):
        dist_start = d[0][1 + k]
        if dist_start != -1:
            dp[1 << k][k] = dist_start

    best = 0
    # empty subset
    if d[0][n-1] != -1 and d[0][n-1] <= T:
        best = 0

    # iterate masks
    for mask in range(full_mask):
        # pruning: if mask has no bits, already checked
        # We'll attempt to compute best using any last; no easy pruning for dp.
        # Transition
        # For each last included
        for last in range(C):
            if not (mask >> last) & 1:
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Finish to goal
            to_goal = d[1 + last][n-1]
            if to_goal != -1:
                total = cur + to_goal
                if total <= T:
                    cnt = mask.bit_count()
                    if cnt > best:
                        best = cnt
            # extend to new candy
            # next bits
            rem = (~mask) & (full_mask - 1)
            while rem:
                nxt = (rem & -rem).bit_length() - 1
                rem -= (1 << nxt)
                dist_last_to_nxt = d[1 + last][1 + nxt]
                if dist_last_to_nxt == -1:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1 << nxt)
                val = cur + dist_last_to_nxt
                if val < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = val

    # Additionally, in case of visiting candies but with redundant possibility:
    # DP already handles ending at goal after last candy.
    # If goal is reachable without candies, best already set to 0.
    # If cannot reach goal at all -> handled above.
    if best == 0:
        # Could be that only empty subset is feasible, then best=0 is fine.
        # But if unreachable overall, already returned -1.
        pass
    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

### Parsed Memory Items

1. Constraint-First Graph Reduction
Description: Replace a large grid with a compact graph of only the “decision-relevant” nodes using shortest-path distances.
<details>
<summary>Content 1</summary>

```text
When the number of special locations is small, run BFS/shortest paths from each special node to compute pairwise distances, then solve the routing/collection problem on this compressed graph. This preserves move counts exactly while enabling exponential DP that would be infeasible on the full grid.
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Reasoning 1</summary>

```text
The fully correct solutions share a consistent high-level structure: (1) reduce the grid problem to a small “special nodes” graph by precomputing shortest-path distances via BFS on the grid, then (2) solve the combinatorial “collect maximum subset under a move budget” using subset DP (bitmask Held–Karp style). The partially correct attempts mostly fail because of incorrect early feasibility logic or incorrect handling of the “must end at goal” constraint (e.g., pruning/feasibility checks that assume direct start→goal reachability implies ability to finish after detours, or subtly mixing unreachable conditions with “detours can help”). Attempts that kept the DP’s objective aligned with the true end condition (DP cost + distance from last collected node to goal ≤ T) succeeded, while ones that used unsafe shortcuts or incomplete state/transition constraints were only partially correct.
```

</details>

2. Align DP Objective With the True Finish Condition
Description: In subset-collection DP, always enforce the final requirement (e.g., “end at goal within T”) in the evaluation step tied to DP states.
<details>
<summary>Content 2</summary>

```text
Use DP to minimize travel cost for each visited subset/order ending at a specific “last” special node, then check feasibility by adding the shortest distance from that last node to the required finish. This avoids missing paths that are feasible only after considering the mandatory final leg.
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Reasoning 2</summary>

```text
The fully correct solutions share a consistent high-level structure: (1) reduce the grid problem to a small “special nodes” graph by precomputing shortest-path distances via BFS on the grid, then (2) solve the combinatorial “collect maximum subset under a move budget” using subset DP (bitmask Held–Karp style). The partially correct attempts mostly fail because of incorrect early feasibility logic or incorrect handling of the “must end at goal” constraint (e.g., pruning/feasibility checks that assume direct start→goal reachability implies ability to finish after detours, or subtly mixing unreachable conditions with “detours can help”). Attempts that kept the DP’s objective aligned with the true end condition (DP cost + distance from last collected node to goal ≤ T) succeeded, while ones that used unsafe shortcuts or incomplete state/transition constraints were only partially correct.
```

</details>

3. Avoid Unsafe Early Impossibility Pruning
Description: Do not declare impossibility based on a single partial shortest-path comparison unless it logically dominates all alternative routes.
<details>
<summary>Content 3</summary>

```text
Early checks like “start→goal is too long” are only valid if they’re proven to be a lower bound on any feasible route. Otherwise, remove/relax that pruning and let the DP/feasibility check determine the true answer.
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Reasoning 3</summary>

```text
The fully correct solutions share a consistent high-level structure: (1) reduce the grid problem to a small “special nodes” graph by precomputing shortest-path distances via BFS on the grid, then (2) solve the combinatorial “collect maximum subset under a move budget” using subset DP (bitmask Held–Karp style). The partially correct attempts mostly fail because of incorrect early feasibility logic or incorrect handling of the “must end at goal” constraint (e.g., pruning/feasibility checks that assume direct start→goal reachability implies ability to finish after detours, or subtly mixing unreachable conditions with “detours can help”). Attempts that kept the DP’s objective aligned with the true end condition (DP cost + distance from last collected node to goal ≤ T) succeeded, while ones that used unsafe shortcuts or incomplete state/transition constraints were only partially correct.
```

</details>

4. Bitmask DP With “Min-Cost Per State” Pattern
Description: For maximizing collected items under a time constraint, track minimal cost for each (subset, last) state and then maximize the subset size among feasible states.
<details>
<summary>Content 4</summary>

```text
Held–Karp style DP (dp[mask][last] = minimal moves to reach last after visiting mask) is robust: transitions add one new item using precomputed pairwise distances, and the maximization happens afterward among states satisfying total cost ≤ T. This separates optimization (minimization DP) from objective selection (max candies).
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Reasoning 4</summary>

```text
The fully correct solutions share a consistent high-level structure: (1) reduce the grid problem to a small “special nodes” graph by precomputing shortest-path distances via BFS on the grid, then (2) solve the combinatorial “collect maximum subset under a move budget” using subset DP (bitmask Held–Karp style). The partially correct attempts mostly fail because of incorrect early feasibility logic or incorrect handling of the “must end at goal” constraint (e.g., pruning/feasibility checks that assume direct start→goal reachability implies ability to finish after detours, or subtly mixing unreachable conditions with “detours can help”). Attempts that kept the DP’s objective aligned with the true end condition (DP cost + distance from last collected node to goal ≤ T) succeeded, while ones that used unsafe shortcuts or incomplete state/transition constraints were only partially correct.
```

</details>

5. Validate Reachability Via Distances, Not Visitation Assumptions
Description: When using shortest-path distances between special nodes, treat unreachable pairs as INF and ensure they are excluded in transitions and feasibility checks.
<details>
<summary>Content 5</summary>

```text
Unreachable special-to-special distances must be filtered during DP updates and final feasibility, otherwise the DP can create nonexistent routes. Using a consistent INF convention across BFS extraction, DP transitions, and final checking prevents these silent correctness gaps.
```

</details>

<details>

```text

The partially correct attempts mostly fail because of incorrect early feasibility logic or incorrect handling of the “must end at goal” constraint (e.g., pruning/feasibility checks that assume direct start→goal reachability implies ability to finish after detours, or subtly mixing unreachable conditions with “detours can help”). Attempts that kept the DP’s objective aligned with the true end condition (DP cost + distance from last collected node to goal ≤ T) succeeded, while ones that used unsafe shortcuts or incomplete state/transition constraints were only partially correct.
```

### System Prompt

You are an expert Python programmer. You will be given a question (problem specification) and will generate a correct Python program that matches the specification and passes all tests.

### User Prompt

```text
### Question:
We have a grid with H rows and W columns.
Let (i,j) denote the square at the i-th row from the top and j-th column from the left.
Each square in the grid is one of the following: the start square, the goal square, an empty square, a wall square, and a candy square.
(i,j) is represented by a character A_{i,j}, and is the start square if A_{i,j}= S, the goal square if A_{i,j}= G, an empty square if A_{i,j}= ., a wall square if A_{i,j}= #, and a candy square if A_{i,j}= o.
Here, it is guaranteed that there are exactly one start, exactly one goal, and at most 18 candy squares.
Takahashi is now at the start square.
He can repeat moving to a vertically or horizontally adjacent non-wall square.
He wants to reach the goal square in at most T moves.
Determine whether it is possible.
If it is possible, find the maximum number of candy squares he can visit on the way to the goal square, where he must finish.
Each candy square counts only once, even if it is visited multiple times.

Input

The input is given from Standard Input in the following format:
H W T
A_{1,1}A_{1,2}\dots A_{1,W}
\vdots
A_{H,1}A_{H,2}\dots A_{H,W}

Output

If it is impossible to reach the goal square in at most T moves, print -1.
Otherwise, print the maximum number of candy squares that can be visited on the way to the goal square, where Takahashi must finish.

Constraints


- 1\leq H,W \leq 300
- 1 \leq T \leq 2\times 10^6
- H, W, and T are integers.
- A_{i,j} is one of S, G, ., #, and o.
- Exactly one pair (i,j) satisfies A_{i,j}= S.
- Exactly one pair (i,j) satisfies A_{i,j}= G.
- At most 18 pairs (i,j) satisfy A_{i,j}= o.

Sample Input 1

3 3 5
S.G
o#o
.#.

Sample Output 1

1

If he makes four moves as (1,1) \rightarrow (1,2) \rightarrow (1,3) \rightarrow (2,3) \rightarrow (1,3), he can visit one candy square and finish at the goal square.
He cannot make five or fewer moves to visit two candy squares and finish at the goal square, so the answer is 1.
Note that making five moves as (1,1) \rightarrow (2,1) \rightarrow (1,1) \rightarrow (1,2) \rightarrow (1,3) \rightarrow (2,3) to visit two candy squares is invalid since he would not finish at the goal square.

Sample Input 2

3 3 1
S.G
.#o
o#.

Sample Output 2

-1

He cannot reach the goal square in one or fewer moves.

Sample Input 3

5 10 2000000
S.o..ooo..
..o..o.o..
..o..ooo..
..o..o.o..
..o..ooo.G

Sample Output 3

18

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    # locate start and goal and candies
    candies = []
    s = g = None
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                s = (i, j)
            elif c == 'G':
                g = (i, j)
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    K = len(candies)
    # nodes: 0 = S, 1..K = candies, K+1 = G
    nodes = [s] + candies + [g]
    N = K + 2  # <= 20

    INF = 10**18

    # BFS from each node to compute shortest distances to all cells.
    # Then dist between nodes only.
    dist_mat = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]

    def bfs(start_idx):
        si, sj = nodes[start_idx]
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        dist[si][sj] = 0
        q.append((si, sj))
        while q:
            i, j = q.popleft()
            dcur = dist[i][j]
            for di, dj in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                ni, nj = i + di, j + dj
                if not (0 <= ni < H and 0 <= nj < W):
                    continue
                if grid[ni][nj] == '#':
                    continue
                if dist[ni][nj] != -1:
                    continue
                dist[ni][nj] = dcur + 1
                q.append((ni, nj))
        # fill dist_mat[start_idx][*] from dist to nodes
        for jdx in range(N):
            ti, tj = nodes[jdx]
            dd = dist[ti][tj]
            if dd != -1:
                dist_mat[start_idx][jdx] = dd

    for i in range(N):
        bfs(i)

    start_to_goal = dist_mat[0][N-1]
    if start_to_goal >= INF:
        print(-1)
        return
    if T < start_to_goal:
        print(-1)
        return

    # We need maximize candies visited (unique) on some walk from S to G within T.
    # With shortest paths between nodes, the minimal move count to visit a set
    # and finish at G will be achieved by some order (TSP-like) using shortest
    # distances between nodes.
    #
    # Since K <= 18, do DP over subsets:
    # dp[mask][last] = minimal moves to start at S, visit candies in mask,
    # and end at candy 'last' (last is index 0..K-1 corresponding to candy node 1+last).
    # We'll later transition to G.
    #
    # If distances are INF for some transitions, those states are invalid.
    full_mask = 1 << K
    dp = [[INF] * K for _ in range(full_mask)]

    # init: from S to each candy
    for c in range(K):
        d = dist_mat[0][1 + c]
        if d < INF:
            dp[1 << c][c] = d

    # transitions
    for mask in range(full_mask):
        for last in range(K):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur >= INF:
                continue
            for nxt in range(K):
                if mask >> nxt & 1:
                    continue
                nd = dist_mat[1 + last][1 + nxt]
                if nd >= INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1 << nxt)
                val = cur + nd
                if val < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = val

    ans = -1
    # For each reachable set, try finish at G from last visited candy
    # Also consider empty set: directly S->G already handled by feasibility.
    for mask in range(full_mask):
        bits = mask.bit_count()
        best = INF
        if mask == 0:
            best = start_to_goal
        else:
            for last in range(K):
                if not (mask >> last) & 1:
                    continue
                cur = dp[mask][last]
                if cur >= INF:
                    continue
                nd = dist_mat[1 + last][N-1]
                if nd >= INF:
                    continue
                best = min(best, cur + nd)
        if best <= T:
            ans = max(ans, bits)

    print(ans)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Baseline generation 2</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sx = sy = gx = gy = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sx, sy = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gx, gy = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    # If S/G positions not found, though constraints guarantee they exist
    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # Build list of important nodes: candies + goal + start
    # We'll compute shortest distances between these points.
    # Indexing:
    # 0..n-1: candies
    # n: goal
    # n+1: start
    points = candies + [(gx, gy), (sx, sy)]
    m = n + 2

    # BFS from each important point to get distances to all cells.
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF] * (H * W) for _ in range(m)]  # too big if H*W large
    # Better: store only distances to important points by doing BFS and sampling.
    # We'll compute distances from each point to all important points only.
    # Use BFS grid distances.
    important_idx = {(x, y): k for k, (x, y) in enumerate(points)}
    important_set = set(important_idx.keys())

    # adjacency moves
    dirs = [(1,0), (-1,0), (0,1), (0,-1)]

    # distances matrix between important nodes
    dm = [[INF]*m for _ in range(m)]
    for a in range(m):
        ax, ay = points[a]
        d = [-1] * (H * W)
        q = deque()
        start_id = ax * W + ay
        d[start_id] = 0
        q.append((ax, ay))
        while q:
            x, y = q.popleft()
            cur = d[x * W + y]
            for dx, dy in dirs:
                nx, ny = x + dx, y + dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    nid = nx * W + ny
                    if d[nid] == -1:
                        d[nid] = cur + 1
                        q.append((nx, ny))
        for b, (bx, by) in enumerate(points):
            val = d[bx * W + by]
            if val != -1:
                dm[a][b] = val

    # Check reachability start->goal at all
    start_i = n + 1
    goal_i = n
    dsg = dm[start_i][goal_i]
    if dsg == INF or dsg > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # We need maximum candies visited.
    # Candy counting constraint:
    # It's possible to revisit/loop if parity matches and within time.
    # For visiting a subset ending at some candy i then to goal:
    # total_min = dist(start->subset order end) + dist(end->goal).
    # But we can add extra cycles to use remaining time if parity allows.
    # For any path between two points, the set of reachable times is:
    # times >= shortest, and parity must match (because grid is unweighted bipartite).
    # When there exists any cycle, we can adjust by even lengths; odd adjustment depends on graph.
    #
    # In grid shortest-path problems, typical AtCoder solution:
    # Use parity of shortest paths; since moves are on bipartite graph,
    # any walk length parity between two vertices is fixed (must match shortest parity).
    # Extra length by looping adds even length (2 steps), so parity remains same.
    # Therefore: feasible iff T >= shortest and (T - shortest) % 2 == 0.
    #
    # We assume walk can be extended by even cycles if needed; in bipartite graphs,
    # you can always add 2-length back-and-forth along any edge as long as you are
    # not forced to stop earlier. Since you must end at goal, you can always insert
    # a 2-step loop anywhere along the path by moving forth and back on an edge
    # that exists on that path (unless path length 0; but then start==goal not possible here).
    # So parity condition is sufficient along the used path.

    # DP over subsets: n <= 18 => 2^n <= 262k
    # dp[mask][last] minimal distance from start to reach 'last' candy
    # having visited candies in mask (mask includes last).
    # We'll compute with Dijkstra-like relaxation on subset graph using shortest paths
    # between important points (candies) and start.
    size = 1 << n
    INF2 = 10**15
    dp = [[INF2]*n for _ in range(size)]
    for i in range(n):
        d = dm[start_i][i]
        if d != INF:
            dp[1<<i][i] = d

    for mask in range(size):
        # prune if no states
        for last in range(n):
            curd = dp[mask][last]
            if curd == INF2:
                continue
            for nxt in range(n):
                if mask >> nxt & 1:
                    continue
                nd = dm[last][nxt]
                if nd == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1<<nxt)
                nv = curd + nd
                if nv < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = nv

    # Also allow visiting zero candies: path start->goal directly.
    best = -1

    def ok_total(minlen):
        return minlen <= T and (T - minlen) % 2 == 0

    if ok_total(dsg):
        best = 0

    # Evaluate subsets ending at any candy
    for mask in range(size):
        k = mask.bit_count()
        if k <= best:
            continue
        # find minimal end->goal route from any last in mask
        ok = False
        for last in range(n):
            if not (mask >> last & 1):
                continue
            d1 = dp[mask][last]
            if d1 == INF2:
                continue
            d2 = dm[last][goal_i]
            if d2 == INF:
                continue
            total = d1 + d2
            if ok_total(total):
                ok = True
                break
        if ok:
            best = k

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

<summary>Baseline generation 3</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
import heapq
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    K = len(candies)  # <= 18
    nodes = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]  # 0..K+1, where K+1 is goal
    N = K + 2

    # Precompute shortest path distances between all special nodes
    # using BFS from each special node (unit grid with walls).
    INF = 10**18
    dist = [[INF]*N for _ in range(N)]

    dirs = [(1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)]

    def bfs_from(src_idx):
        di, dj = nodes[src_idx]
        q = deque()
        seen = [[-1]*W for _ in range(H)]
        seen[di][dj] = 0
        q.append((di, dj))
        while q:
            i, j = q.popleft()
            dcur = seen[i][j]
            for di2, dj2 in dirs:
                ni, nj = i + di2, j + dj2
                if 0 <= ni < H and 0 <= nj < W and grid[ni][nj] != '#':
                    if seen[ni][nj] == -1:
                        seen[ni][nj] = dcur + 1
                        q.append((ni, nj))
        # fill dist to other nodes
        for t_idx, (ti, tj) in enumerate(nodes):
            if seen[ti][tj] != -1:
                dist[src_idx][t_idx] = seen[ti][tj]

    for i in range(N):
        bfs_from(i)

    # If goal unreachable from start within T -> -1 (still must ensure feasibility of any solution)
    if dist[0][N-1] > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies (bitmask), compute shortest time:
    # dp[mask][last] = min distance from start, visiting candies in mask, ending at candy last
    # We'll also allow moving through any cells; distances between special nodes are shortest.
    # Complexity: 2^K * K <= 2^18*18 ~ 4.7M states.
    M = 1 << K
    dp = [ [INF]*K for _ in range(M) ]
    for i in range(K):
        d = dist[0][1+i]
        if d < INF:
            dp[1<<i][i] = d

    # Iterate masks
    for mask in range(M):
        # skip masks with no finite dp
        # optional: check quickly
        row = dp[mask]
        # find any finite
        if min(row) == INF:
            continue
        for last in range(K):
            cur = row[last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # go to next candy
            rem = ((M-1) ^ mask)
            while rem:
                lsb = rem & -rem
                nxt = (lsb.bit_length() - 1)
                rem -= lsb
                nd = dist[1+last][1+nxt]
                if nd == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | lsb
                val = cur + nd
                if val < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = val

    # Evaluate best candy count among subsets that can reach goal within T
    ans = -1
    for mask in range(M):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        best_to_goal = INF
        for last in range(K):
            d = dp[mask][last]
            if d == INF:
                continue
            dg = dist[1+last][N-1]
            if dg == INF:
                continue
            best_to_goal = min(best_to_goal, d + dg)
        # Also consider empty subset: direct start->goal
        if mask == 0:
            best_to_goal = dist[0][N-1]
        if best_to_goal <= T:
            if cnt > ans:
                ans = cnt

    print(ans)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()

<summary>Baseline generation 4</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
import heapq
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline
    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)
    # Nodes: 0 = S, 1..n = candies, n+1 = G
    nodes = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    m = n + 2

    INF = 10**30

    def dijkstra(start_idx):
        sr0, sc0 = nodes[start_idx]
        dist = [[INF] * W for _ in range(H)]
        dist[sr0][sc0] = 0
        pq = [(0, sr0, sc0)]
        while pq:
            d, r, c = heapq.heappop(pq)
            if d != dist[r][c]:
                continue
            if d > T:  # pruning: only matters up to T
                continue
            for dr, dc in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                    nd = d + 1
                    if nd < dist[nr][nc]:
                        dist[nr][nc] = nd
                        heapq.heappush(pq, (nd, nr, nc))
        return dist

    # Compute pairwise shortest path distances among nodes
    # Use Dijkstra from each node (at most 20 nodes)
    dist_node = [[INF] * m for _ in range(m)]
    dists = []
    for i in range(m):
        di = dijkstra(i)
        dists.append(di)
    for i in range(m):
        for j in range(m):
            r, c = nodes[j]
            dist_node[i][j] = dists[i][r][c]

    # If goal unreachable at all within T, still answer might be -1 because we must finish at goal.
    base = dist_node[0][m-1]
    if base > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies that can be visited starting from S and ending at a candy
    # Total candies <= 18 => 2^n <= 262144
    # dp[mask][i] = min moves to start at S, visit exactly candies in mask,
    # and currently at candy i (where i in [0..n-1], mask includes i). Minimization.
    # Then answer: max popcount(mask) such that exists i with dp[mask][i] + dist(candy i -> G) <= T.
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        d = dist_node[0][i+1]
        if d <= T:
            dp[1 << i][i] = d

    # Transitions
    for mask in range(size):
        # quick skip: if no reachable endpoint
        # Find any i reachable (optional)
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # Try to go to next candy j
            # Next mask = mask | (1<<j)
            for j in range(n):
                if mask >> j & 1:
                    continue
                nd = cur + dist_node[i+1][j+1]
                if nd <= T and nd < dp[mask | (1 << j)][j]:
                    dp[mask | (1 << j)][j] = nd

    # Evaluate best
    best = -1
    # Also allow visiting no candies: just S->G
    if base <= T:
        best = 0

    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= best:
            continue
        ok = False
        for i in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][i]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            endd = cur + dist_node[i+1][m-1]
            if endd <= T:
                ok = True
                break
        if ok:
            best = cnt

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    si = sj = gi = gj = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                si, sj = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gi, gj = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    C = len(candies)
    if C == 0:
        # Just check reachability within T
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        dq = deque([(si, sj)])
        dist[si][sj] = 0
        dirs = [(1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)]
        while dq:
            x, y = dq.popleft()
            for dx, dy in dirs:
                nx, ny = x + dx, y + dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    if dist[nx][ny] == -1:
                        dist[nx][ny] = dist[x][y] + 1
                        dq.append((nx, ny))
        d = dist[gi][gj]
        if d == -1 or d > T:
            print(-1)
        else:
            print(0)
        return

    # BFS from each special point (S, candies, G) to get pairwise shortest distances
    points = [(si, sj)] + candies + [(gi, gj)]
    P = 1 + C + 1

    def bfs_from(src):
        sx, sy = src
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        dq = deque([(sx, sy)])
        dist[sx][sy] = 0
        dirs = [(1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)]
        while dq:
            x, y = dq.popleft()
            for dx, dy in dirs:
                nx, ny = x + dx, y + dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    if dist[nx][ny] == -1:
                        dist[nx][ny] = dist[x][y] + 1
                        dq.append((nx, ny))
        return dist

    dists = []
    for p in points:
        dmat = bfs_from(p)
        dists.append(dmat)

    INF = 10**18

    # Build distance matrix between special points
    dist_sp = [[INF] * P for _ in range(P)]
    for i in range(P):
        xi, yi = points[i]
        for j in range(P):
            xj, yj = points[j]
            d = dists[i][xj][yj]
            if d != -1:
                dist_sp[i][j] = d

    # Quick feasibility: if even shortest S->G > T then impossible (but DP will also handle)
    if dist_sp[0][P-1] > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies: dp[mask][last] = min moves to start at S,
    # visit candies in mask, and end at candy last (index in 0..C-1),
    # where "last" is included in mask.
    # Complexity: O( C^2 * 2^C ) with C<=18 => OK.
    size = 1 << C
    dp = [[INF] * C for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize transitions from S to each reachable candy
    for i in range(C):
        d = dist_sp[0][1 + i]
        if d != INF:
            dp[1 << i][i] = d

    # Transitions among candies
    for mask in range(size):
        for last in range(C):
            if not (mask & (1 << last)):
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            for nxt in range(C):
                if mask & (1 << nxt):
                    continue
                nd = dist_sp[1 + last][1 + nxt]
                if nd == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1 << nxt)
                val = cur + nd
                if val < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = val

    # Also allow masks empty? We can visit 0 candies: just check S->G.
    best = -1
    if dist_sp[0][P-1] <= T:
        best = 0

    # For each state ending at a candy, add distance to G
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= best:
            # cannot beat best in count, but might still if best=-1; handle already
            pass
        for last in range(C):
            if not (mask & (1 << last)):
                continue
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            to_goal = dist_sp[1 + last][P - 1]
            if to_goal == INF:
                continue
            total = cur + to_goal
            if total <= T:
                if cnt > best:
                    best = cnt

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

<summary>Baseline generation 6</summary>

```text
```python
import sys, heapq

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    s = g = None
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                s = (i, j)
            elif c == 'G':
                g = (i, j)
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    # Dijkstra from a given set of sources over the grid (walls blocked)
    def dijkstra_from_source(src):
        INF = 10**30
        dist = [[INF] * W for _ in range(H)]
        si, sj = src
        dist[si][sj] = 0
        pq = [(0, si, sj)]
        while pq:
            d, i, j = heapq.heappop(pq)
            if d != dist[i][j]:
                continue
            for di, dj in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                ni, nj = i + di, j + dj
                if 0 <= ni < H and 0 <= nj < W and grid[ni][nj] != '#':
                    nd = d + 1
                    if nd < dist[ni][nj]:
                        dist[ni][nj] = nd
                        heapq.heappush(pq, (nd, ni, nj))
        return dist

    # Compute shortest paths between S, G, and each candy using Dijkstra from each.
    points = [s] + candies + [g]
    n = len(candies)
    # indices: 0=S, 1..n=candies, n+1=G
    dist_between = [[10**30]*(n+2) for _ in range(n+2)]

    for a in range(n+2):
        dist_grid = dijkstra_from_source(points[a])
        for b in range(n+2):
            bi, bj = points[b]
            dist_between[a][b] = dist_grid[bi][bj]

    # If G unreachable at all, answer -1
    base = dist_between[0][n+1]
    if base > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # Standard trick for "visit as many nodes (<=18) as possible with travel constraint":
    # Use meet-in-the-middle on shortest path metric.
    # We can model as: start at S, finish at G, may visit subset of candies at most once in terms of ordering,
    # but path distances satisfy triangle inequality (shortest paths on grid), so best to visit candies in some order.
    #
    # We'll solve with DP over subsets using TSP-like DP since n<=18.
    # Complexity O(n^2 * 2^n) ~ 18^2*262k ~ ok.
    #
    # dp[mask][i] = min distance to start at S, visit exactly candies in mask, and end at candy i (i in mask).
    # Answer: max popcount(mask) such that min_i dp[mask][i] + dist(i->G) <= T.

    # Map candy index k (0..n-1) to point index 1+k.
    INF = 10**30
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF]*n for _ in range(size)]

    # init: from S to each candy
    for k in range(n):
        d = dist_between[0][1+k]
        if d <= T:
            dp[1<<k][k] = d

    # transitions
    for mask in range(size):
        # pruning: if mask has no bits, skip
        # (dp[mask][*] might still be INF; that's fine)
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # try add next
            rem = ((size-1) ^ mask)
            # iterate bits in rem
            while rem:
                lsb = rem & -rem
                nxt = (lsb.bit_length() - 1)
                rem -= lsb
                nmask = mask | (1<<nxt)
                nd = cur + dist_between[1+last][1+nxt]
                if nd < dp[nmask][nxt] and nd <= T:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = nd

    best = 0
    # also allow visiting no candy
    if base <= T:
        best = 0

    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= best:
            continue
        # compute minimal completion distance to G
        ok = False
        for last in range(n):
            if not (mask & (1<<last)):
                continue
            d = dp[mask][last]
            if d == INF:
                continue
            if d + dist_between[1+last][n+1] <= T:
                ok = True
                break
        if ok:
            best = cnt

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()

<summary>Baseline generation 7</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

INF = 10**18

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().rstrip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    # Build list of points: start + candies + goal
    points = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    n = len(points)  # <= 20 (start + <=18 + goal)

    # Compute shortest path distances between all pairs using BFS from each point
    # Only passable cells are anything except '#'
    passable = [[c != '#' for c in row] for row in grid]

    def bfs(si, sj):
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        dist[si][sj] = 0
        q.append((si, sj))
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            d = dist[r][c] + 1
            if r > 0 and passable[r-1][c] and dist[r-1][c] == -1:
                dist[r-1][c] = d
                q.append((r-1, c))
            if r+1 < H and passable[r+1][c] and dist[r+1][c] == -1:
                dist[r+1][c] = d
                q.append((r+1, c))
            if c > 0 and passable[r][c-1] == -1 and passable[r][c-1]:
                dist[r][c-1] = d
                q.append((r, c-1))
            if c+1 < W and passable[r][c+1] and dist[r][c+1] == -1:
                dist[r][c+1] = d
                q.append((r, c+1))
        return dist

    # Pairwise distances matrix
    D = [[INF] * n for _ in range(n)]
    for i in range(n):
        dist_grid = bfs(points[i][0], points[i][1])
        for j in range(n):
            d = dist_grid[points[j][0]][points[j][1]]
            if d != -1:
                D[i][j] = d

    start_idx = 0
    goal_idx = n - 1
    candy_count = n - 2

    # If goal unreachable from start at all within T, answer is -1
    if D[start_idx][goal_idx] == INF or D[start_idx][goal_idx] > T:
        # still could be possible by visiting candies (but must reach goal at end)
        # however if start->goal unreachable, going via others could make it reachable,
        # so we can't early return solely on that.
        pass

    # Dijkstra on state: (mask, u) where u is last visited point among candies (1..candy_count)
    # We want max candies visited such that we can end at goal within T.
    # Use best[mask] for minimal distance to reach some last candy? We'll use DP by last node.
    m = candy_count
    if m == 0:
        ans = D[start_idx][goal_idx]
        print(-1 if ans == INF or ans > T else 0)
        return

    size = 1 << m
    # best[mask][u] where u in [0..m-1] corresponds to candy point index 1+u
    best = [[INF] * m for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize: go from start to each candy
    for u in range(m):
        d = D[start_idx][1 + u]
        if d != INF:
            best[1 << u][u] = d

    # Transition among candies
    for mask in range(size):
        for u in range(m):
            cur = best[mask][u]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # try add v
            rem = (~mask) & (size - 1)
            # iterate v bits
            b = rem
            while b:
                lsb = b & -b
                v = (lsb.bit_length() - 1)
                nb = mask | lsb
                nd = cur + D[1 + u][1 + v]
                if D[1 + u][1 + v] != INF and nd < best[nb][v]:
                    best[nb][v] = nd
                b -= lsb

    # Also allow finishing at goal without visiting any candy
    ans = -1
    if D[start_idx][goal_idx] != INF and D[start_idx][goal_idx] <= T:
        ans = 0

    # Evaluate best for all masks and ending at goal
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= ans:
            continue
        for u in range(m):
            d = best[mask][u]
            if d == INF:
                continue
            # need last -> goal
            dg = D[1 + u][goal_idx]
            if dg == INF:
                continue
            if d + dg <= T:
                ans = max(ans, cnt)

    print(ans)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

<summary>Baseline generation 8</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
import heapq

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline
    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().rstrip("\n")) for _ in range(H)]

    INF = 10**18

    # Find start/goal and candies
    sx = sy = gx = gy = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sx, sy = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gx, gy = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    k = len(candies)  # <= 18
    # If start/goal missing shouldn't happen due to statement
    points = [(sx, sy)] + candies + [(gx, gy)]  # indices: 0..k+1
    npts = k + 2

    # BFS (0-1 not needed; unweighted grid) from each point to get distances to all cells
    # Use early exit to only collect distances to points.
    def bfs_from(start):
        dist = [[-1]*W for _ in range(H)]
        q = [(start[0], start[1])]
        dist[start[0]][start[1]] = 0
        head = 0
        while head < len(q):
            x, y = q[head]
            head += 1
            nd = dist[x][y] + 1
            for dx, dy in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                nx, ny = x + dx, y + dy
                if 0 <= nx < H and 0 <= ny < W and dist[nx][ny] == -1 and grid[nx][ny] != '#':
                    dist[nx][ny] = nd
                    q.append((nx, ny))
        return dist

    # Dist matrix between points
    dmat = [[INF]*npts for _ in range(npts)]
    for i, (px, py) in enumerate(points):
        dist = bfs_from((px, py))
        for j, (qx, qy) in enumerate(points):
            if dist[qx][qy] != -1:
                dmat[i][j] = dist[qx][qy]

    # quick check reachability S->G within T
    if dmat[0][k+1] > T:
        # still might be possible with candies, so don't early return
        pass

    # If k is 0
    if k == 0:
        print(-1 if dmat[0][1] > T else 0)
        return

    # DP over subsets: dp[mask][last] minimal distance from start (point 0)
    # to visit candies in mask and end at candy last (0..k-1 for candies).
    # Transition using distances between points.
    # Then add distance from last candy to goal point (k+1).
    # Complexity: O(2^k * k^2) manageable for k<=18.
    size = 1 << k
    dp = [[INF]*k for _ in range(size)]

    # init
    for i in range(k):
        di = dmat[0][i+1]
        if di < INF:
            dp[1<<i][i] = di

    # iterate masks
    for mask in range(size):
        # for each last
        for last in range(k):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # try add next
            for nxt in range(k):
                if mask & (1<<nxt):
                    continue
                nd = cur + dmat[last+1][nxt+1]
                if dmat[last+1][nxt+1] >= INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1<<nxt)
                if nd < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = nd

    ans = -1
    # evaluate best mask: minimal total distance = min_last dp[mask][last] + dist(last, goal)
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= ans:
            continue
        best = INF
        for last in range(k):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            to_goal = dmat[last+1][k+1]
            if to_goal >= INF:
                continue
            total = cur + to_goal
            if total < best:
                best = total
        # allow going to goal without visiting any candy? corresponds to mask=0
        if mask == 0:
            best = dmat[0][k+1]
        if best <= T:
            ans = cnt

    print(ans if ans != -1 else -1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

<summary>Baseline generation 9</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline

    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().rstrip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sy = sx = gy = gx = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sy, sx = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gy, gx = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18
    # Special nodes: 0 = S, 1..n = candies, n+1 = G
    coords = [(sy, sx)] + candies + [(gy, gx)]
    m = n + 2

    # BFS from each special node to compute shortest distances to all cells
    def bfs(start_i, start_j):
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        dq = deque([(start_i, start_j)])
        dist[start_i][start_j] = 0
        while dq:
            y, x = dq.popleft()
            d = dist[y][x]
            for dy, dx in ((1,0), (-1,0), (0,1), (0,-1)):
                ny, nx = y + dy, x + dx
                if 0 <= ny < H and 0 <= nx < W and grid[ny][nx] != '#':
                    if dist[ny][nx] == -1:
                        dist[ny][nx] = d + 1
                        dq.append((ny, nx))
        return dist

    # Precompute pairwise distances among special nodes
    dmat = [[10**18] * m for _ in range(m)]
    for i in range(m):
        dist = bfs(coords[i][0], coords[i][1])
        for j in range(m):
            ty, tx = coords[j]
            dv = dist[ty][tx]
            if dv != -1:
                dmat[i][j] = dv

    if dmat[0][m-1] > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # DP over subsets of candies:
    # dp[mask][last] = min moves to start at S, visit candies in mask, end at candy last (last is index 1..n)
    # We'll store only candies indices 0..n-1 mapping to node 1..n.
    INF = 10**18
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(size)]

    # Initialize from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        w = dmat[0][i+1]
        if w <= T:  # only relevant if within T by the time we possibly reach G, but safe prune
            dp[1 << i][i] = w

    # Transitions
    for mask in range(size):
        # skip impossible masks quickly if all dp are INF
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # extend to next candy
            for nxt in range(n):
                if mask >> nxt & 1:
                    continue
                nd = cur + dmat[last+1][nxt+1]
                if nd < dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt] and nd <= T:
                    dp[mask | (1 << nxt)][nxt] = nd

    # Compute best candies count achievable with total <= T and finishing at G
    # Also consider visiting zero candies (just S->G)
    best = 0
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        # Try finishing from any last candy in mask
        ok = False
        for last in range(n):
            if mask >> last & 1:
                dist_to_g = dmat[last+1][m-1]
                if dist_to_g != 10**18:
                    total = dp[mask][last] + dist_to_g
                    if dp[mask][last] != INF and total <= T:
                        ok = True
                        break
        if ok:
            if cnt > best:
                best = cnt

    # Also check zero-candy path (already ensured reachable)
    # If best is 0 but reachable only via candies subset could not exist; it's fine.
    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

<summary>Baseline generation 10</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

def solve():
    input = sys.stdin.readline
    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sy = sx = gy = gx = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            c = grid[i][j]
            if c == 'S':
                sy, sx = i, j
            elif c == 'G':
                gy, gx = i, j
            elif c == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    n = len(candies)  # <= 18

    # BFS from each special node (S, each candy, G) to compute distances through open cells
    specials = [(sy, sx)] + candies + [(gy, gx)]
    m = n + 2  # S + candies + G

    # helper BFS
    def bfs_from(start):
        dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque()
        si, sj = start
        dist[si][sj] = 0
        q.append((si, sj))
        while q:
            i, j = q.popleft()
            d = dist[i][j]
            nd = d + 1
            for di, dj in ((1,0), (-1,0), (0,1), (0,-1)):
                ni, nj = i + di, j + dj
                if 0 <= ni < H and 0 <= nj < W and grid[ni][nj] != '#':
                    if dist[ni][nj] == -1:
                        dist[ni][nj] = nd
                        q.append((ni, nj))
        return dist

    dists = []
    for k in range(m):
        dists.append(bfs_from(specials[k]))

    # distances from node k to node l
    # node indices: 0 = S, 1..n = candies, n+1 = G
    def dist_between(a, b):
        (ai, aj) = specials[a]
        (bi, bj) = specials[b]
        return dists[a][bi][bj]

    # Quick feasibility: shortest path S->G must be <= T
    sg = dist_between(0, n+1)
    if sg == -1 or sg > T:
        print(-1)
        return

    # Build complete graph distances among specials (excluding unreachable pairs)
    INF = 10**18
    w = [[INF] * m for _ in range(m)]
    for a in range(m):
        for b in range(m):
            if a == b:
                w[a][b] = 0
            else:
                da = dist_between(a, b)
                if da != -1:
                    w[a][b] = da

    # We want max candies visited; classic "TSP with time limit" using bitmask DP.
    # dp[mask][last] = minimum distance to start at S, visit candies in mask, end at candy 'last'
    # where last is in [0..n-1] corresponding to candy index (mask bits).
    # At end, add distance from last to G.
    #
    # Time constraint includes finishing at G; moves count includes all edges lengths.
    #
    # Complexity: n<=18 => 2^n * n fits.
    size = 1 << n
    dp = [[INF] * n for _ in range(size)]
    dp[0] = [0] * n  # not used, but keep safe; we'll never transition from dp[0][last] meaningfully

    # Initialize transitions from S to each candy
    for i in range(n):
        di = w[0][i+1]
        if di != INF:
            dp[1 << i][i] = di

    # Iterate masks
    for mask in range(size):
        for last in range(n):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # try add next candy
            rem = (~mask) & (size - 1)
            while rem:
                nxt_bit = rem & -rem
                rem -= nxt_bit
                nxt = (nxt_bit.bit_length() - 1)
                nd = cur + w[last+1][nxt+1]
                if nd < dp[mask | nxt_bit][nxt]:
                    dp[mask | nxt_bit][nxt] = nd

    # Also allow taking zero candies: just S->G
    best = -1

    # check mask with last -> G
    # Also consider masks with at least one candy. We'll compute max candies such that min distance <= T.
    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        # compute minimal total time ending at G with this mask (ending at any last)
        ok = False
        min_total = INF
        if mask == 0:
            min_total = sg
        else:
            for last in range(n):
                if (mask >> last) & 1:
                    cur = dp[mask][last]
                    if cur == INF:
                        continue
                    back = w[last+1][n+1]
                    if back == INF:
                        continue
                    total = cur + back
                    if total < min_total:
                        min_total = total
        if min_total <= T:
            if cnt > best:
                best = cnt

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```

### Augmented

### System Prompt

```text
You are an expert Python programmer. You will be given a question (problem specification) and will generate a correct Python program that matches the specification and passes all tests.
```

### User Prompt

```text
Before solving, consider these reusable insights from prior analysis:

  1. Constraint-First Graph Reduction: Replace a large grid with a compact graph of only the “decision-relevant” nodes using shortest-path distances.
     When the number of special locations is small, run BFS/shortest paths from each special node to compute pairwise distances, then solve the routing/collection problem on this compressed graph. This preserves move counts exactly while enabling exponential DP that would be infeasible on the full grid.
  2. Align DP Objective With the True Finish Condition: In subset-collection DP, always enforce the final requirement (e.g., “end at goal within T”) in the evaluation step tied to DP states.
     Use DP to minimize travel cost for each visited subset/order ending at a specific “last” special node, then check feasibility by adding the shortest distance from that last node to the required finish. This avoids missing paths that are feasible only after considering the mandatory final leg.
  3. Avoid Unsafe Early Impossibility Pruning: Do not declare impossibility based on a single partial shortest-path comparison unless it logically dominates all alternative routes.
     Early checks like “start→goal is too long” are only valid if they’re proven to be a lower bound on any feasible route. Otherwise, remove/relax that pruning and let the DP/feasibility check determine the true answer.
  4. Bitmask DP With “Min-Cost Per State” Pattern: For maximizing collected items under a time constraint, track minimal cost for each (subset, last) state and then maximize the subset size among feasible states.
     Held–Karp style DP (dp[mask][last] = minimal moves to reach last after visiting mask) is robust: transitions add one new item using precomputed pairwise distances, and the maximization happens afterward among states satisfying total cost ≤ T. This separates optimization (minimization DP) from objective selection (max candies).
  5. Validate Reachability Via Distances, Not Visitation Assumptions: When using shortest-path distances between special nodes, treat unreachable pairs as INF and ensure they are excluded in transitions and feasibility checks.
     Unreachable special-to-special distances must be filtered during DP updates and final feasibility, otherwise the DP can create nonexistent routes. Using a consistent INF convention across BFS extraction, DP transitions, and final checking prevents these silent correctness gaps.

Apply these insights to the problem below.

### Question:
We have a grid with H rows and W columns.
Let (i,j) denote the square at the i-th row from the top and j-th column from the left.
Each square in the grid is one of the following: the start square, the goal square, an empty square, a wall square, and a candy square.
(i,j) is represented by a character A_{i,j}, and is the start square if A_{i,j}= S, the goal square if A_{i,j}= G, an empty square if A_{i,j}= ., a wall square if A_{i,j}= #, and a candy square if A_{i,j}= o.
Here, it is guaranteed that there are exactly one start, exactly one goal, and at most 18 candy squares.
Takahashi is now at the start square.
He can repeat moving to a vertically or horizontally adjacent non-wall square.
He wants to reach the goal square in at most T moves.
Determine whether it is possible.
If it is possible, find the maximum number of candy squares he can visit on the way to the goal square, where he must finish.
Each candy square counts only once, even if it is visited multiple times.

Input

The input is given from Standard Input in the following format:
H W T
A_{1,1}A_{1,2}\dots A_{1,W}
\vdots
A_{H,1}A_{H,2}\dots A_{H,W}

Output

If it is impossible to reach the goal square in at most T moves, print -1.
Otherwise, print the maximum number of candy squares that can be visited on the way to the goal square, where Takahashi must finish.

Constraints


- 1\leq H,W \leq 300
- 1 \leq T \leq 2\times 10^6
- H, W, and T are integers.
- A_{i,j} is one of S, G, ., #, and o.
- Exactly one pair (i,j) satisfies A_{i,j}= S.
- Exactly one pair (i,j) satisfies A_{i,j}= G.
- At most 18 pairs (i,j) satisfy A_{i,j}= o.

Sample Input 1

3 3 5
S.G
o#o
.#.

Sample Output 1

1

If he makes four moves as (1,1) \rightarrow (1,2) \rightarrow (1,3) \rightarrow (2,3) \rightarrow (1,3), he can visit one candy square and finish at the goal square.
He cannot make five or fewer moves to visit two candy squares and finish at the goal square, so the answer is 1.
Note that making five moves as (1,1) \rightarrow (2,1) \rightarrow (1,1) \rightarrow (1,2) \rightarrow (1,3) \rightarrow (2,3) to visit two candy squares is invalid since he would not finish at the goal square.

Sample Input 2

3 3 1
S.G
.#o
o#.

Sample Output 2

-1

He cannot reach the goal square in one or fewer moves.

Sample Input 3

5 10 2000000
S.o..ooo..
..o..o.o..
..o..ooo..
..o..o.o..
..o..ooo.G

Sample Output 3

18

### Format: Read the inputs from stdin solve the problem and write the answer to stdout (do not directly test on the sample inputs). Enclose your code within delimiters as follows. Ensure that when the python program runs, it reads the inputs, runs the algorithm and writes output to STDOUT.
```python
# YOUR CODE HERE
```

### Answer: (use the provided format with backticks)
```

<details>
<summary>Augmented generation 1</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

INF = 10**18

def bfs_dist(grid, H, W, sr, sc):
    dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
    q = deque([(sr, sc)])
    dist[sr][sc] = 0
    while q:
        r, c = q.popleft()
        d = dist[r][c] + 1
        if d >= T_global + 1:  # slight speed-up, distances beyond T are not needed for feasibility
            # still need correctness because we only ever compare against <=T,
            # but we don't need exact distances beyond T.
            # We'll cap exploration.
            continue
        for dr, dc in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
            nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
            if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#':
                if dist[nr][nc] == -1:
                    dist[nr][nc] = d
                    q.append((nr, nc))
    return dist

def solve():
    global T_global
    input = sys.stdin.readline
    H, W, T_global = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    rs = cs = rg = cg = -1
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            ch = grid[i][j]
            if ch == 'S':
                rs, cs = i, j
            elif ch == 'G':
                rg, cg = i, j
            elif ch == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    K = len(candies)  # <= 18
    # nodes: 0 = start, 1..K = candies, K+1 = goal
    nodes = [(rs, cs)] + candies + [(rg, cg)]
    N = K + 2

    # Compute pairwise shortest path distances between all nodes (only for special nodes)
    # Using BFS from each special node. Unreachable => INF.
    dmat = [[INF] * N for _ in range(N)]
    for i in range(N):
        si, sj = nodes[i]
        dist = bfs_dist(grid, H, W, si, sj)
        for j in range(N):
            ti, tj = nodes[j]
            dd = dist[ti][tj]
            if dd != -1 and dd <= T_global:
                dmat[i][j] = dd
            elif dd != -1:
                dmat[i][j] = dd  # still might be needed when combining; but feasibility always uses <=T
                # if dd > T, it's effectively unusable; keep exact only if computed by BFS.
                # Our BFS was capped by T, so dd might be -1 for >T; handle with INF already.
    # The cap in bfs_dist would mark >T as unreachable, which is fine because any route with
    # a segment > T can never be part of a feasible total path (nonnegative lengths).
    # Therefore treating them as INF preserves correctness for <=T feasibility.

    start_to_goal = dmat[0][K+1]
    if start_to_goal == INF:
        print(-1)
        return

    # Held-Karp style:
    # dp[mask][last] = minimal moves to start at S, visit candies in mask (mask over K bits),
    # ending at candy index (0..K-1) corresponding to "last".
    # Then total = dp + dist from last to goal <= T to be feasible.
    # Also allow mask=0: end directly at goal.
    size_mask = 1 << K
    dp = [[INF] * K for _ in range(size_mask)]

    # Initialize: visit single candy last
    for c in range(K):
        dist_sc = dmat[0][c+1]
        if dist_sc != INF:
            dp[1 << c][c] = dist_sc

    # transitions
    for mask in range(size_mask):
        # iterate last
        for last in range(K):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # try to go to new candy nxt
            # If we keep exact costs capped by T, we can prune using <=T
            for nxt in range(K):
                if mask & (1 << nxt):
                    continue
                seg = dmat[last+1][nxt+1]
                if seg == INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1 << nxt)
                ncost = cur + seg
                if ncost <= T_global and ncost < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = ncost

    best = -1

    # mask=0 feasible?
    if start_to_goal <= T_global:
        best = 0

    # For all masks, check feasibility of ending at goal
    # Only consider masks where any dp exists.
    for mask in range(size_mask):
        # count candies visited
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        if cnt <= best:
            continue
        for last in range(K):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            to_goal = dmat[last+1][K+1]
            if to_goal == INF:
                continue
            if cur + to_goal <= T_global:
                if cnt > best:
                    best = cnt
                break

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Augmented generation 2</summary>

```text
```python
import sys
from collections import deque

INF = 10**18

def bfs_dist(grid, H, W, src_idx, src_r, src_c, special_pos):
    """
    BFS from (src_r, src_c) over non-wall cells.
    Returns list d[k] = distance from src to special_pos[k] (only for specials), INF if unreachable.
    """
    dist = [[-1] * W for _ in range(H)]
    q = deque()
    dist[src_r][src_c] = 0
    q.append((src_r, src_c))
    d = [INF] * len(special_pos)
    # src is always a special; map its coordinate to index
    while q:
        r, c = q.popleft()
        cur = dist[r][c]
        # If this cell is a special, record distance
        # (We compare to special coordinates via a set mapping for speed)
        # We'll instead use a dictionary mapping for positions.
        # This function is called only with grid size up to 300, so we can check using a map.
        nd = None
        # nothing
        for dr, dc in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
            nr, nc = r + dr, c + dc
            if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#' and dist[nr][nc] == -1:
                dist[nr][nc] = cur + 1
                q.append((nr, nc))
    # Fill distances to specials using their coordinates
    for k, (rr, cc) in enumerate(special_pos):
        val = dist[rr][cc]
        if val != -1:
            d[k] = val
    return d

def solve():
    sys.setrecursionlimit(1_000_000)
    input = sys.stdin.readline
    H, W, T = map(int, input().split())
    grid = [list(input().strip()) for _ in range(H)]

    sr = sc = gr = gc = None
    candies = []
    for i in range(H):
        for j in range(W):
            if grid[i][j] == 'S':
                sr, sc = i, j
            elif grid[i][j] == 'G':
                gr, gc = i, j
            elif grid[i][j] == 'o':
                candies.append((i, j))

    # specials: start + candies + goal
    m = len(candies)
    # If no candies, just check direct reachability.
    if m == 0:
        # BFS from start to goal
        dist = [[-1]*W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque([(sr, sc)])
        dist[sr][sc] = 0
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            for dr, dc in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                nr, nc = r+dr, c+dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#' and dist[nr][nc] == -1:
                    dist[nr][nc] = dist[r][c] + 1
                    q.append((nr, nc))
        ans = dist[gr][gc]
        if ans != -1 and ans <= T:
            print(0)
        else:
            print(-1)
        return

    # indices:
    # 0: start, 1..m: candies, m+1: goal
    special_pos = [(sr, sc)] + candies + [(gr, gc)]
    K = m + 2

    # Compute all-pairs distances among specials via BFS from each special.
    # Complexity: K*(H*W) where K<=20 => OK.
    dist_mat = [[INF]*K for _ in range(K)]
    for i in range(K):
        r0, c0 = special_pos[i]
        # BFS distances from special i
        dist = [[-1]*W for _ in range(H)]
        q = deque([(r0, c0)])
        dist[r0][c0] = 0
        while q:
            r, c = q.popleft()
            for dr, dc in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                nr, nc = r+dr, c+dc
                if 0 <= nr < H and 0 <= nc < W and grid[nr][nc] != '#' and dist[nr][nc] == -1:
                    dist[nr][nc] = dist[r][c] + 1
                    q.append((nr, nc))
        for j in range(K):
            rr, cc = special_pos[j]
            val = dist[rr][cc]
            if val != -1:
                dist_mat[i][j] = val

    # If start cannot reach goal at all, still might be possible via candies.
    # We'll handle via DP feasibility with final leg.

    # Held-Karp style DP:
    # dp[mask][last] = minimal moves to start at start(0),
    # visit candies indicated by mask, and end at candy index last (0..m-1 corresponds to special node 1+last).
    # Transition uses distances between specials.
    size = 1 << m
    dp = [[INF]*m for _ in range(size)]

    # init: visit single candy k
    for k in range(m):
        d = dist_mat[0][1+k]
        if d < INF:
            dp[1<<k][k] = d

    # transitions
    for mask in range(size):
        for last in range(m):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            # try go to next candy nxt
            rem = (~mask) & (size-1)
            while rem:
                lsb = rem & -rem
                nxt = (lsb.bit_length() - 1)
                rem -= lsb
                d_between = dist_mat[1+last][1+nxt]
                if d_between >= INF:
                    continue
                nmask = mask | (1<<nxt)
                nc = cur + d_between
                if nc < dp[nmask][nxt]:
                    dp[nmask][nxt] = nc

    # Also allow visiting zero candies: end at goal directly.
    # For each state (mask,last), check if can finish at goal within T:
    # total = dp + dist(last_candy, goal).
    # Take maximum candies visited.
    best = -1

    # zero candies
    d0 = dist_mat[0][m+1]
    if d0 < INF and d0 <= T:
        best = 0

    for mask in range(size):
        cnt = mask.bit_count()
        # We can early skip if cnt <= best? not safe because best could be -1; but still skip if cnt<=best always safe.
        if cnt <= best:
            continue
        for last in range(m):
            cur = dp[mask][last]
            if cur == INF:
                continue
            to_goal = dist_mat[1+last][m+1]
            if to_goal >= INF:
                continue
            if cur + to_goal <= T:
                best = cnt
                break

    print(best)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    solve()
